**75.** **Jeremy McNichols - TB:** Rookie Jeremy McNichols found himself in an interesting spot after the 2017 Draft, as Doug Martin is suspended to start the season and the only thing standing in front of him and playing time are Charles Sims and Jacquizz Rodgers. McNichols is a talented rookie who is very worth a late round flier, especially if you own Martin.

## **_WR:_**


**1.** **Antonio Brown - Pit:** Brown had the second most receptions in the NFL last year despite seeing constant double or triple teams throughout the entirety of the season. He is an elite player who also returns punts (if your league counts return points at all), and should be off the board in the first half of every first round with confidence. He is poised for another huge season here in 2017.

| Rank  | Player Name  | Targets       | Receptions         | Receiving Yards | Receiving TD’s  | Red Zone Targets  | Red Zone Receptions  | Red Zone Receiving TD's  |
| ------------- | ------------- |:-------------:| -----:| -----:| -----:| -----:| -----:| -----:|
| **1** | **_Antonio Brown_** | 155     | 106 | 1,284 | 12 | 15 | 9 | 4 |



**2.** **Odell Beckham, Jr. - NYG:** Odell Beckham receives more competition for targets this season in the form of veteran red zone vulture Brandon Marshall and huge rookie tight end-wide receiver combo player Evan Engram. Beckham, however, should partially counteract this dip in targets with an increase in productivity, as defenses will not be able to allocate as much attention to him as they have in years past. The Giants attempted almost 600 passes last season, meaning work will be bountiful enough to fulfill Beckham’s first round fantasy potential. Take him with confidence.

| Rank  | Player Name  | Targets       | Receptions         | Receiving Yards | Receiving TD’s  | Red Zone Targets  | Red Zone Receptions  | Red Zone Receiving TD's  |
| ------------- | ------------- |:-------------:| -----:| -----:| -----:| -----:| -----:| -----:|
| **2** | **_Odell Beckham, Jr._** | 169     | 101 | 1,367 | 10 | 21 | 9 | 5 |



**3.** **Julio Jones - Atl:** Julio Jones is an elite talent that could - like the rest of the Atlanta offense - see a statistical dip this season due to the departure of Kyle Shanahan to San Francisco. Jones has played all 16 games only twice in his six-year NFL career, and new offensive coordinator Steve Sarkisian has often had a more conservative passing tendency than the deeper-targeting offenses that have brought Jones more success. Despite the potential for regression in yardage, Jones is still a first round prospect in fantasy and will likely be again among the top receivers at the end of the season.

| Rank  | Player Name  | Targets       | Receptions         | Receiving Yards | Receiving TD’s  | Red Zone Targets  | Red Zone Receptions  | Red Zone Receiving TD's  |
| ------------- | ------------- |:-------------:| -----:| -----:| -----:| -----:| -----:| -----:|
| **3** | **_Julio Jones_** | 129     | 83 | 1,409 | 6 | 9 | 4 | 2 |



**4.** **Mike Evans - TB:** Evans saw an absurd 175 targets last season, and that is bound to elevate anyone to success in fantasy, but take note of the 96 receptions he had. If his catch percentage were even slightly higher, he would’ve been the pick of the year in last seasons’ fantasy drafts. While the Buccaneers added deep threat DeSean Jackson and rookie tight end OJ Howard this season, that should only open up coverage for Evans and allow him to catch more of those targets. Evans is one of the better available selections outside of the surefire top picks this year.

| Rank  | Player Name  | Targets       | Receptions         | Receiving Yards | Receiving TD’s  | Red Zone Targets  | Red Zone Receptions  | Red Zone Receiving TD's  |
| ------------- | ------------- |:-------------:| -----:| -----:| -----:| -----:| -----:| -----:|
| **4** | **_Mike Evans_** | 175     | 96 | 1,321 | 12 | 17 | 8 | 7 |



**5.** **AJ Green - Cin:** AJ Green is one of the most consistent wide receivers in football. Last season - when he played only 10 games - was the first in which he did not have over 1,000 yards in his entire six year career…and he still had 964. Green should benefit from the addition of speedster John Ross, as opposing defenses will now be forced to divert some attention to the home run threat as well as the pure receiving ability of Green. Green is a top level fantasy wide receiver, and should not fall too far this season in fantasy drafts.

| Rank  | Player Name  | Targets       | Receptions         | Receiving Yards | Receiving TD’s  | Red Zone Targets  | Red Zone Receptions  | Red Zone Receiving TD's  |
| ------------- | ------------- |:-------------:| -----:| -----:| -----:| -----:| -----:| -----:|
| **5** | **_AJ Green_** | 100     | 66 | 964 | 4 | 9 | 7 | 2 |



**6.** **Jordy Nelson - GB:** Nelson was first in [ESPN's consistency ratings](http://www.espn.com/fantasy/football/story/_/page/consistency2016/final-2016-fantasy-football-consistency-ratings) in regards to start percentage, making him the most reliable receiver in fantasy last season. His value comes from not only catching passes from Aaron Rodgers, but the trust that Rodgers has in Nelson. Nelson had 29 red zone targets last season, including 15 inside 10, and posted 9 TD’S from inside the ten yard line. Nelson is a top level WR1 who tends to fall a bit too far in drafts, so if you’re at the end of the first/beginning of the second round, don’t hesitate to snag Nelson.

| Rank  | Player Name  | Targets       | Receptions         | Receiving Yards | Receiving TD’s  | Red Zone Targets  | Red Zone Receptions  | Red Zone Receiving TD's  |
| ------------- | ------------- |:-------------:| -----:| -----:| -----:| -----:| -----:| -----:|
| **6** | **_Jordy Nelson_** | 152     | 97 | 1,257 | 14 | 29 | 19 | 11 |



**7.** **Michael Thomas - NO:** Michael Thomas was the surprise of the fantasy world last season. He saw 11 targets from inside the ten yard line, and scored on 6 of them. He had at least 5 catches in 11 games (out of the 15 he played), and proved to be a reliable target in the league’s most potent passing offense as the Saints were the only team to throw for over 5,000 yards last year. With Brandin Cooks off to New England, Thomas now becomes the undisputed number one receiver in New Orleans. Mike Clay at ESPN noted that since Sean Payton and Drew Brees arrived in New Orleans in 2006, the target share (percentage of total team targets) of the team's top wide receiver during their 11 years of work is as follows: 20, 23, 19, 20, 20, 17, 20, 18, 16, 20, 19. Look for Thomas to have another explosive year as the targets - and the attention from opposing defenses - increase.

| Rank  | Player Name  | Targets       | Receptions         | Receiving Yards | Receiving TD’s  | Red Zone Targets  | Red Zone Receptions  | Red Zone Receiving TD's  |
| ------------- | ------------- |:-------------:| -----:| -----:| -----:| -----:| -----:| -----:|
| **7** | **_Michael Thomas_** | 122     | 92 | 1,137 | 9 | 19 | 13 | 7 |



**8.** **TY Hilton - Ind:** Per last year’s [strength of schedule metrics](http://www.espn.com/blog/nflnation/post/_/id/234722/2017-nfl-strength-of-schedule), the Colts have easiest schedule in 2017. TY Hilton averaged 117.9 receiving yards in games the Colts won (per Matthew Berry at ESPN), and has proven to be Luck’s favorite target with over 1,000 yards receiving in each of the last four seasons. Hilton is extremely reliable, and proves to be an reliable top end fantasy wide receiver year in and year out. He’s a WR1 without a doubt.

| Rank  | Player Name  | Targets       | Receptions         | Receiving Yards | Receiving TD’s  | Red Zone Targets  | Red Zone Receptions  | Red Zone Receiving TD's  |
| ------------- | ------------- |:-------------:| -----:| -----:| -----:| -----:| -----:| -----:|
| **8** | **_TY Hilton_** | 156     | 91 | 1,448 | 6 | 13 | 8 | 2 |



**9.** **Dez Bryant - Dal:** While the Cowboys as a whole had a very successful season last year, Bryant seemed to underperform for fantasy purposes. He has not played a full season since 2014, and had been held to 1,197 yards receiving in 2015 and 2016 combined. He is alleged to be a full go this season, and could thus be a nice sleeper pick towards the end of the second or through the third round, but it’s risky to rely on him as your WR1 at this point. High upside, but take with caution.

| Rank  | Player Name  | Targets       | Receptions         | Receiving Yards | Receiving TD’s  | Red Zone Targets  | Red Zone Receptions  | Red Zone Receiving TD's  |

| **9** | **_Dez Bryant_** | 97     | 50 | 796 | 8 | 12 | 6 | 5 |



**10.** **Amari Cooper - Oak:** Cooper had 0 red zone TD’s last season on 13 red zone targets, but has been dominant despite only scoring 11 times in his first two seasons. However, he has had 1,000 yards in each of those seasons. He’s an effective targets and yards receiver in fantasy in the same mold as Julio Jones, and any touchdowns can be seen as a major bonus. With Carr signed to a large extension this offseason and the addition of Marshawn Lynch to the running game, expect Cooper to again put up large numbers through the air. He’s a reliable WR1 to own if you cannot snag one of the top level guys.

| Rank  | Player Name  | Targets       | Receptions         | Receiving Yards | Receiving TD’s  | Red Zone Targets  | Red Zone Receptions  | Red Zone Receiving TD's  |

| **10** | **_Amari Cooper_** | 132     | 83 | 1,153 | 5 | 13 | 5 | 0 |



**11.** **Doug Baldwin - Sea:** Baldwin has had over 1,000 yards in each of the last two season and added a combined 172 receptions in that span to boot. While those are fringe WR1/WR2 numbers, Matthew Berry at ESPN noted that Russell Wilson's passing yardage total has increased every season of his career, and the addition of Eddie Lacy may only aid this fact. That said, don’t reach for Baldwin too high in drafts - as his volume in a potent passing attack is solid enough to be a low level WR1 or top level WR2 - but he is a reliable pick in the later second or third round.

**12.** **DeAndre Hopkins - Hou:** Hopkins suffered from mediocre QB play last season, and had merely 1 red zone TD last season despite having 9 red zone targets. While Houston’s quarterback situation should be monitored closely in regards to selecting Hopkins in fantasy, what’s indisputable is the talent that Hopkins possesses on an every down basis. His 150 targets is staggering, and he should improve on his meager catch percentage whether Tom Savage or rookie DeShaun Watson is under center this year. Hopkins has high upside based on his draft position, but don’t reach for him too early.

| Rank  | Player Name  | Targets       | Receptions         | Receiving Yards | Receiving TD’s  | Red Zone Targets  | Red Zone Receptions  | Red Zone Receiving TD's  |

**13.** **Demaryius Thomas - Den:** Thomas has had over 1,000 yards receiving every season since 2011, and four of those five were seasons of 1,300 or more yards. Granted, Peyton Manning is a step or two up from Trevor Siemian/Paxton Lynch, but Thomas should prove to yet again be an important figure in the passing game. While touchdowns may be difficult to come by in Denver’s mediocre offense, volume keeps Thomas as a solid WR2 for fantasy purposes.

**14.** **Brandin Cooks - NE:** The center of offseason trade hype this season, Cooks sets off for defending champion New England, where he can pair with arguably one of the greatest quarterbacks of all time in Tom Brady. Brady led the NFL in vertical yards per attempt last season, which is ideal for Cooks’ skill set, and gives the receiver huge upside. While target competition and New England’s frequent decision to employ a short, quick passing game have been frequent antagonists to fantasy production, look for Cooks to defy the odds and have a big season while opening up New England’s already championship caliber offense.

**15.** **Sammy Watkins - Buf:** Sammy Watkins is extremely injury prone, but he is only 24 and is currently entering a contract year. He is averaging 7.8 targets per game (27 percent share) during the 32 games in which he has played at least 70 percent of the pass-play snaps (per Mike Clay at ESPN), exemplifying his value to the Buffalo offense as a whole. While the addition of rookie Zay Jones gives Watkins some competition for targets, the removal of Rex Ryan from the coaching staff should provide Buffalo with more passing attempts overall. Watkins is a risky WR2 in fantasy this season, but has WR1 upside if he can stay healthy.

**16.** **Allen Robinson - Jac:** Robinson was a highly touted fantasy asset last season, ranked [13th overall and just behind Le'Veon Bell](http://www.espn.com/fantasy/football/story/_/id/16287927/2016-fantasy-football-rankings-top-300) before the year started, but disappointed all who drafted him while posting less than 900 receiving yards. Robinson had all the opportunity in the world, as he was 6th in the NFL in targets last year, 10th in the NFL in red zone targets, and 6th in the NFL in red zone touchdowns, per Field Yates at ESPN. Robinson should fall in drafts this season due to his regression last year, but the addition of Leonard Fournette should bolster the Jaguars offense as a whole, and Robinson could be the main beneficiary. He’s a high upside WR2 this season.

**17.** **Alshon Jeffery - Phi:** Jeffery should be one of the biggest beneficiaries of fantasy production due to team change in 2017. Joining the Eagles as Carson Wentz’s immediate number one target, Jeffery is sure to see a lot of work in an offense that threw the 6th most passes in the NFL last season (609), and the addition of LeGarrette Blount should help to open up the receiving game a little more than usual. Jeffery is a high upside WR2 in fantasy leagues this season, but keep in mind that he is quite injury prone (played two full seasons in his five year career).

**18.** **Terrelle Pryor - Was** Terrelle Pryor has a great season last year as he posted over 1,000 yards in Cleveland with a starting quarterback combination of Josh McCown, Robert Griffin III, and Cody Kessler. He now joins a Redskins offense that lost both DeSean Jackson and Pierre Garcon in the offseason, and is looking for another passing threat to roll out besides Jamison Crowder and Jordan Reed. Matthew Berry at ESPN notes that in the past two seasons, only Matt Ryan has a better deep completion percentage than Kirk Cousins, which could pay off for Pryor. He’s a WR2 for fantasy purposes.

**19.** **Davante Adams - GB:** Aaron Rodgers alone gives Adams a boost in fantasy circles, but he is a reliable receiver in his own right in one of the league’s best offenses. Adams saw 10 targets from inside the 10 last season and scored on 5 of them, and proved to be a valuable asset overall for Green Bay with 12 total receiving touchdowns. While often benefiting from less coverage as he is playing opposite of Jordy Nelson, Adams has the potential to put up big numbers while still providing a solid level of consistency. He’s a good WR2 to own in fantasy leagues.

**20.** **Keenan Allen - LAC:** Keenan Allen is an productive fantasy wide receiver when healthy, but in the mere four seasons since he’s left college, he has had a torn PCL, ACL, broken collarbone, lacerated kidney, and other smaller injuries holding him to 9 total games n the last two seasons combined. He also has a lot more receiving competition this year in Mike Williams and an emerging Hunter Henry, but Allen has proven himself as one of Rivers’ favorite targets when he is one the field. Allen is a risky player due to durability concerns, but don’t sleep on the talent here. If he stays healthy, he could be a low end WR2. But, that’s a big if.

**21.** **Michael Crabtree - Oak:** Crabtree finished tied for 10th in targets last season with 145, and looks to build on his 1,000 yard season last year in a dangerous Oakland passing attack. The addition of Marshawn Lynch adds an element to the running game that is impossible for opposing defenses to ignore, and Crabtree could benefit greatly from this. He is the Raiders’ main red zone threat - seeing 21 red zone targets last year - and is still a solid WR2 in fantasy leagues.

**22.** **Golden Tate - Det:** Golden Tate is a high volume receiver in an offense that ranked 11th in the NFL last season in total passing attempts (594). He has seen at least 128 targets every season since coming to Detroit in 2014, and is one of Matthew Stafford’s most reliable receivers. Per Mike Clay at ESPN, he has been on the field for at least 87 percent of his team's snaps (one season with Seattle, three with Detroit) and handled at least 21 percent of the targets in four consecutive seasons. Tate’s score last season could have been much higher if he had reeled in more targets in the red zone, as he caught 1 touchdown inside the 20 despite 17 total red zone targets. With touchdown vulture Anquan Boldin gone and the volume to still be plentiful, look for Tate to be a borderline WR2 in PPR leagues this season, especially if his touchdown total goes up (it should).

**23.** **Emmanuel Sanders - Den:** Sanders suffered from poor QB play last season (as did the Broncos as a whole), but is also very reliable in fantasy. He has missed only 1 game in his 3 seasons in Denver, and Matthew Berry at ESPN noted that Sanders has 16 different games with at least 20 PPR points since 2014, and only Antonio Brown, Julio Jones, Odell Beckham Jr have more of those games in that span. While Trevor Siemian/Paxton Lynch limited him to a 2016 catch rate of only 58.1% and only 8 games of 50 or more yards receiving, Sanders still put up over 1,000 yards due to his high volume and target share (139 targets on the season). Sanders can be a solid WR2 in PPR leagues, but is worth slightly less in leagues that score nothing for receptions.

**24.** **Jarvis Landry - Mia:** Jarvis Landry put up over 1,100 yards last season on 136 targets despite playing in a Miami offense with the second lowest amount of passing attempts in the entire NFL (477). The resigning of Kenny Stills and offseason talk-up of Devante Parker gives Landry target competition that he is not used to, but it should also take some attention off of him, as well. Touchdowns could be hard to come by, as Jay Ajayi has proven to be a powerful runner and was given the 9th most carries on the season despite not solidifying the starting job until week 5, but Landry is a monster in PPR leagues and is thus a WR2 in such.

**25.** **Tyreek Hill - KC:** An intriguing prospect last season, Tyreek Hill burst onto the scene as an effective receiver, rusher, and return man. Jeremy Maclin is out in KC, and Hill now moves into the spotlight of the passing offense along with tight end Travis Kelce. How he will be utilized this season remains to be seen, but expect Hill to be reliant on a few different things, including (but not limited to) deep or long distance receptions/touchdowns, sporadically long distance rushing attempts, and the occasional return touchdown. Hill varies widely by league in terms of fantasy value, as he saw only 83 targets last season, but that number figures to go up with Maclin’s departure. Take a special note of Hill if you play in leagues that count A. Big play bonuses (in any fashion), or B. Return yards (in any fashion). Otherwise, don’t reach for him too high…at least until we hear anything about his potential usage from Kansas City.

| **25** | **_Tyreek Hill_** | 83     | 61 | 593 | 6 | 13 | 10 | 3 |



**26.** **Martavis Bryant - Pit:** Bryant is coming off of a yearlong suspension, but his return is widely anticipated. Per Mike Clay at ESPN, he has been on the field for at least 70 percent of the team's pass plays during 12 of his 24 career games (11 of which came in 2015). During those 12 showings, Bryant handled 9.5 targets per game (25 percent share). Matthew Berry noted that last season Steelers wide receivers not named Antonio Brown combined for 102 catches, 1,481 yards and 11 touchdowns. The 15 touchdowns Bryant has in his 21 career games shows that Ben Roethlisberger trusts Bryant as a target, and thus Bryant should not be left to far in fantasy drafts, pending a solid preseason/not getting into trouble. He could have a big season, and is a more attractive pick than many other receivers.

| ------------- | ------------- |:-------------:| -----:| -----:| -----:| -----:| -----:| -----:|
| **26** | **_Martavis Bryant_** | 0     | 0 | 0 | 0 | 0 | 0 | 0 |



**27.** **Larry Fitzgerald - Ari:** Larry Fitzgerald has consistently been of the most reliable wide receivers in fantasy football. He has missed 6 games in his entire career (13 seasons), and has had over 1,000 yards in 8 of those seasons (including the last two). With the Cardinals passing attack being such a significant part of their game plan in 2016 (646 passing attempts, 3rd in the NFL), expect Fitzgerald to again be a reliable fantasy receiver - especially in PPR formats. John Brown returning to health should help to draw a bit of attention away from Fitzgerald, and we can expect to see Fitzgerald to remain in his usage of 150 targets last season. He’s a reliable WR2/WR3 (more valuable in PPR leagues) that is worth taking over a riskier option at this point in the draft.

| **27** | **_Larry Fitzgerald_** | 150     | 107 | 1,023 | 6 | 20 | 13 | 4 |



**28.** **Julian Edelman - NE:** Edelman has been a favorite target of Tom Brady’s for some time, as he has seen at least 134 targets in 3 of the last 4 seasons, save for the 2015 season in which he played only 9 games due to injury. Edelman is a high floor, low ceiling prospect who does much better in PPR formats, as touchdowns in the New England offense are tough to come by for wide receivers. With at least 972 yards in each of the 3 full seasons he has played out of the last four, Edelman remains a solid PPR target and WR3 in non-PPR scoring leagues.

**29.** **Jamison Crowder - Was:** Jamison Crowder burst onto the fantasy scene last season, with 97 targets despite competing for passes with DeSean Jackson, Pierre Garcon, and Jordan Reed. Jackson and Garcon are gone this season, meaning there are 203 targets up for grabs this season in Washington between the two. The addition of Terrelle Pryor should actually help Crowder’s fantasy potential, as defensive attention will be less focused on him in the wake of the departure of the aforementioned Jackson and Garcon. Crowder is a great PPR selection as a WR3, especially if your league counts return yards, as he also returned some punts last season.

**30.** **Stefon Diggs - Min:** The conservative nature of the Vikings offense has hampered Diggs for fantasy purposes, but he still put up 903 yards last season on 111 targets. While red zone targets are hard to come by (12 on the season) and touchdowns to wide receivers are scarce, Diggs is the number one receiver in an offense that threw the 12th most passes in the NFL last season at 588. Volume makes Diggs a WR3 for fantasy purposes, but don’t reach for him, as touchdowns have proven difficult to come by in the conservative Minnesota offense.

**31.** **Willie Snead - NO:** Willie Snead had a solids season last year playing as the third receiver in New Orleans’ league leading passing attack, and his fantasy stock should improve with the trade of Brandin Cooks to the Patriots. While Ten Ginn comes to town in his place, Ginn is more of a straight line speedster, and Snead should now be number two behind Michael Thomas in Drew Brees’ 2017 passing spray chart. Due to this, Snead should see his targets increase a bit from the 104 he had last season, and is a good WR3 to own this year in what should be another big season from Drew Brees and the Saints passing attack.

**32.** **Donte Moncrief - Ind:** Donte Moncrief is a difficult projection to make in any preseason ranking, as his touchdown potential and injury potential go hand in hand to form a dangerous predictive duo. Moncrief had 6 red zone TD’s on 10 red zone targets last season…on six total targets. Per Mike Clay at ESPN, he has had 11 TD’s in 15 games with Andrew Luck in last two seasons, and was on the field for at least 70 percent of the team's pass plays in 18 games…and he averaged 7.8 targets per game (21 percent share) during that span. Moncrief is a risky pick with high upside, and is a great selection as a WR3 or flex player with upside.

**33.** **Kelvin Benjamin - Car:** Kelvin Benjamin had over 900 yards and 7 receiving touchdowns in a stumbling Carolina offense after his missed 2015 season, but it is difficult to gauge how his 2017 production will pan out. The Panthers added Christian McCaffrey and Curtis Samuel - who are both competent rushers and receivers - in the NFL Draft this year, and much is to be discovered about the roses each will play in the offense. Benjamin, however, is still the number one receiver in a Carolina offense that should regress this season, making him a nice upside fantasy play as a WR3 this year.

**34.** **DeSean Jackson - TB:** Jackson joins a rebooted Tampa Bay offense that is looking a lot more dangerous than in previous years, and could benefit from the diverted attention. Jackson is a deep ball receiver, and thus a boom or bust fantasy prospect, but has proven to be effective in his time in the NFL. While those in leagues that target big plays in the form of extra points should pay extra attention to Jackson, those in regular PPR or regular non-PPR leagues should at least be aware of his weekly variance in point production before drafting him. Jackson is a solid WR3, as during his good weeks he will put up WR1 numbers. The bust weeks, however, are what keeps him at WR3.

**35.** **Brandon Marshall - NYG:** Brandon Marshall switches sides in New York this season, joining a Giants passing attack that is known for rolling out three receiver formations more than any other team in recent years. Thus, Marshall should get a ton of work despite target competition from Odell Beckham, Jr., Sterling Shepard, and rookie tight end Evan Engram. Per Matthew Berry at ESPN, Marshall leads all NFL wideouts with 35 red zone scores since 2012, and the big wideout looks to be Manning’s prime target in the end zone this season, as well. While he will no doubt be playing second fiddle to OBJ (and reaping the benefits of less attention from defenses along with it), do not sleep on Marshall in fantasy drafts this season. He could get a lot of scores as well as targets. He’s a high upside WR3.

**36.** **Pierre Garcon - SF:** Garcon moves to the 49ers this season to reunite with Kyle Shanahan, his former coordinator in Washington, with whom he had great success. Garcon led the NFL in receptions (with 113) the last time he played with Shanahan in 2013, and his target share should be large enough again this season to have him right back there again. Despite a seemingly lackluster offense, Brian Hoyer is a decent quarterback who can deliver reliable results when healthy. He should be able to get Garcon the ball often this season, and garbage time can do wonders for fantasy wide receivers when the Niners get down early. He’s much more valuable in PPR leagues, but Garcon is a high upside WR3 this season as he heads the 49ers receiving corps.

**37.** **Eric Decker - Ten:** Decker signed a late contract with Tennessee after being released by the Jets, and could see major value in fantasy as a possession receiver in Tennessee, with the emerging Marcus Mariota under center. Matthew Berry at ESPN noted that Decker was third in the NFL in red zone receptions and second in red zone touchdowns from 2012 until 2015, and Mariota is well known for his red zone prowess. While Decker has a lot of potential, the target competition in Tennessee is fierce this season, returning the pass catchers from last year while adding new ones in the draft (including 5th overall pick Corey Davis). He could be a reliable receiver this season, but it is too variable at this point in the offseason to say for sure what Decker’s role will be. He’s still worth a look in fantasy as a flex play in drafts.

**38.** **Jeremy Maclin - Bal:** Maclin had a tough season in Kansas City last year, putting up only 536 yards on 76 targets, but could see a big improvement this season in the league’s most  pass heavy offense over the last two seasons. With Mike Wallace and Danny Woodhead to take targets and defensive attention away, look for Maclin’s numbers to increase significantly this season from his down year in KC. He’s a solid flex player this year, and could be even higher if he reels in a nice catch percentage for his (presumed) plethora of targets.

**39.** **DeVante Parker - Mia:** Parker is an intriguing player this season in fantasy circles, and part of that has stemmed from the uptalk he has received from both players and coaches down in Miami. He actually had an equivalent starting percentage to Brandin Cooks and Golden Tate last year according to [ESPN's consistency ratings](http://www.espn.com/fantasy/football/story/_/page/consistency2016/final-2016-fantasy-football-consistency-ratings), and that was in a season in which he was only targeted 90 times. While the resigned Kenny Stills should take away targets from Parker, Jarvis Landry will draw away both targets and defensive coverage. Parker could be a solid WR3 this season, especially if he starts to see more red zone targets (2 of his 4 touchdowns came in the red zone).

**40.** **Tyrell Wiliams - LAC:** Tyrell Williams was 18th in PPR fantasy points among wide receivers and had over 1,000 yards last year for a struggling Chargers team. While the team drafted rookie Mike Williams (who is currently dealing with an injury) and has another end zone target in Hunter Henry, Tyrell Williams preserves his role on the team after a breakout season last year. Tyrell Williams should be a valuable later round pick, as he established himself as a reliable target behind the injury prone Keenan Allen.

**41.** **Cameron Meredith - Chi:** Cameron Meredith was a surprise on the Bears’ offense last season, putting up 888 yards on 96 targets in a subpar offense. The Bears passing attack as a whole should be slightly better this season, with Mike Glennon coming in to throw and Kevin White having the entire offseason to get healthy. Meredith could reap the benefits of this, as the targets have to go somewhere. Touchdowns will be hard to come by, but he’s a top receiver on a poor offense, and is thus worth a spot on your roster as a WR3 or flex player.

**42.** **John Brown - Ari:** John Brown should be returning fully healthy this season, and he could be a very sneaky fantasy pick due to it. In his last healthy season (2015), he had 6 catches over 40 yards, and Mike Clay at ESPN pointed out that Brown was averaging 6.9 targets per game (20 percent share) during the 35 games in which he has played at least 70 percent of the pass-play snaps. As the number two receiver in an Arizona passing offense that threw 646 passes last season (3rd most), Brown is an intriguing sleeper pick this year. He’s got WR3 upside, and is a great value down this low.

**43.** **Kenny Britt - Cle:** The new starting receiver in Cleveland, Britt’s landing spot alone could result in enough targets for a good season. Terrell Pryor had over 1,000 yards with much worse QB play (and a worse line blocking for him) than Britt will have, and the entire Browns offense should have a much different look this season than in years past. Britt won’t blow the doors off the stadium, but he should be another reliable play as a flex or low level WR3 this season due to volume alone.

**44.** **Randall Cobb - GB:** As a starting receiver in one of the best offenses in football, it is interesting to observe the path that Randall Cobb’s stats have taken over the past few seasons. His 1,287 yard breakout in 2014 was followed by 829 yards in 2015 and a mere 610 last season, and it is difficult to pinpoint why. He’s a tough asset to locate this season in fantasy drafts, but he’s worth a late round flier due to his solidified place in the Green Bay offense and the fact that he has shown flashes of greatness before. Don’t trust him as anything higher than a flex play, but he’s a flex play that could have some good upside.

**45.** **Mike Wallace - Bal:** No team has attempted more pass attempts than the Ravens in each of the past two seasons, and Steve Smith has been replaced by Jeremy Maclin. Danny Woodhead has also been added to the backfield, but all of this should only benefit Mike Wallace. Matthew Berry at ESPN noted that in the 8 seasons he has played in the NFL, Wallace has posted a top-30 WR fantasy finish 7 times. That is simply astounding for a player who was known as a speedster early in his career and seems to have fallen off the face of the fantasy earth in recent years. Despite that, Wallace put up over 1,000 yards last season on 117 targets. Flacco should be throwing early and often again this season, and look for Wallace to be a main beneficiary. Despite the fact that he is not being drafted like it, Wallace is a good flex/WR3 - especially in PPR leagues.

**46.** **Corey Coleman - Cle:** Coleman broke his hand halfway through the season (in practice) and missed a chunk of his rookie year due to such. He showed some flashes of greatness that made him the first wide receiver taken in 2016, but he reeled in only 33 of 74 targets on the year. As much of that can be said of the quarterbacks under center as it can be about Coleman, but the QB position should (hopefully) be improved over last year and Coleman’s numbers should jump to solid flex play or low level WR3 numbers. He is a good pickup in leagues that count big play bonuses, as speed is one of his major strongpoints.

**47.** **Adam Thielen - Min:** Adam Thielen is probably most remembered for his 202 yard, 2 touchdown performance in the fantasy championship week last season, but he should be looked upon this year as a reliable target in a conservative Minnesota offense. Bradford developed a nice rapport with Thielen throughout the course of the season, and expect his targets to be well over 100 this season working opposite of Stefon Diggs - who should draw the majority of the attention from opposing secondaries. He’s a decent flex play this year due to target volume, especially in PPR leagues, but expect his up and down trend of scoring on a weekly basis to continue.

**48.** **Corey Davis - Ten** Davis is a dynamic rookie who should be fully healthy and ready to go following offseason surgery, and joins a dangerous Titans offense that could turn a lot of heads this season. Davis could become an immediate contributor in Tennessee, and could be a late round steal in fantasy leagues - if he falls that far. Expect there to be a lot of hype around Corey Davis, especially after solid rookie performances in recent years (think Michael Thomas), but he’s a great upside pick to add to your group of wide receivers towards the middle to later end of the draft.

**49.** **Rishard Matthews - Ten:** Rishard Matthews had one of the most interesting fantasy seasons of all wide receivers last year. He had no more than 4 catches in any single game until week 9, but did well on the year as a whole with 9 receiving touchdowns and 945 yards. Matthews is in an interesting situation in Tennessee, where he now faces target competition from newcomers Eric Decker and rookie sensation Corey Davis, as well as other rookies in the form of Taywan Taylor and Jonnu Smith. Don’t expect a repeat of last season for Matthews in the touchdown department, but he could approach the 800-900 yard range again. He’s a good bench receiver for your fantasy team.

**50.** **Quincy Enunwa - NYJ:** Quincy Enunwa is the current number one receiver for the New York Jets, as both Brandon Marshall and Eric Decker are gone and QB position should be (slightly) improved with McCown starting (for now). Enunwa put up respectable numbers last year on 106 targets, and he could surpass those numbers this year without Marshall and Decker in the mix. His touchdowns will most likely not improve due to the mediocre quality of the Jets offense as a whole, but Enunwa could be a sleeper pick later in drafts due to his presumed volume.

**51.** **Jordan Matthews - Phi** Recent additions to the Philadelphia passing attack could prove to be more beneficial than detrimental to Matthews this season. Alshon Jeffery and Torrey Smith - as well as running back LeGarrette Blount - join an Eagles offense that threw 609 passes last season, 6th most in the NFL. While that number should dip a bit due to the addition of Blount, expect there to be plenty of targets to go around, and a lot of attention now diverted away from Matthews and onto Jeffery and deep threat Torrey Smith. Matthews is a good value deep into drafts that could be left to fall, and should still see enough targets to be fantasy relevant as a flex play or potentially even a WR3 if he can get a few more looks in the end zone.

**52.** **Marvin Jones - Det:** Marvin Jones exploded for 408 yards receiving in the first 3 games of last year, but didn’t have another 100 yard game for the rest of the season. While he had a solid 103 targets in a respectable Detroit passing offense, he shouldn’t be counted on to produce those numbers from the early weeks of 2016 again. He can be a reliable flex receiver in PPR leagues, but don’t count on him for all that much more than that.

Drew Brees could send some of the thousand plus yards he’s fed Cooks in the each of the last two years to Ginn, but Michael Thomas is the #1 receiver here. Ginn is most valuable in leagues that count big play bonuses, and less valued in PPR leagues.

His red zone targets (12, on which he scored 6 of his 8 touchdowns) should also be poached by both Marshall and Engram. Regardless, he will be on the field often, and is thus a worthy late round look in fantasy drafts.

**57.** **Robert Woods - LAR:** Robert Woods could be this year’s Kenny Britt - the only guy to throw to for the LA Rams. He was respectable on his mere 74 targets in Buffalo last year, and should improve in an offense where he is featured more often. Woods is falling vey late, and, as a starting receiver, is worth the upside.

**58.** **Kevin White - Chi:** White is falling incredibly far for someone of his caliber and team situation. Alshon Jeffery has moved on, and Cameron Meredith is the only other receiver standing in White’s way in Chicago this season. The only thing he has to do is remain healthy - which he has proven as an insurmountable task since being drafted 7th overall just two years ago. White is a great sleeper pick deep into drafts, pending he stays healthy.

**59.** **Kenny Stills - Mia:** Stills was extended in the offseason after a 9 touchdown performance last season, but it was fairly surprising considering his mere 81 targets. He shouldn’t repeat those touchdowns and is still behind Jarvis Landry and Devante Parker on the depth chart, but he’s a decent flier to take later in the draft in hoping that the Dolphins extended him for a reason.

**60.** **Tyler Lockett - Sea:** Lockett saw only 67 targets last season, but should be more involved (if he can remain healthy) in a solid Seattle passing attack. He is a very talented player that is a danger with the ball in his hands, and could be worth a lot higher than the spot he currently holds. That said, don’t reach too high for him. He’s a risky bench receiver.

He’s got decent upside in PPR leagues, but not much more than that.

**62.** **JJ Nelson - Ari:** JJ Nelson should be impeded by the healthy return of John Brown, and when looking at his stats from last season it is apparent that he is not a reliable fantasy asset. Four of his six touchdowns came in the red zone, and he caught only 34 passes across the entire season. He is not exactly a reliable fantasy receiver this year.

**63.** **Marqise Lee - Jac:** Marqise Lee quietly had 105 targets last season, and put up 851 yards to go along with 3 touchdowns. The Jaguars now have a running game behind Leonard Fournette, and Lee could improve along with the offense as a whole.  While Blake Bortles’ struggles haven’t helped Lee much and his tendency to get injured doesn’t help him either, Lee is a good sleeper pick late in drafts his season.

**64.** **Cole Beasley - Dal:** Cole Beasley caught 75 of his 98 targets, and had the highest red zone touchdown conversion rate in the NFL by putting up 5 scores on 8 targets. Mike Clay at ESPN noted that Beasley played 58 percent of Dallas' snaps, including 75 percent of pass plays, and handled 20 percent of the targets. Beasley is a solid flex play in PPR leagues, but little more than a bench player otherwise.

**65.** **John Ross - Cin:** - John Ross will line up across from AJ Green and give the Bengals the deep threat they have not had in recent seasons. While there is competition for targets in Cincinnati from tight end Tyler Eifert, Tyler Boyd, and veteran Brandon LaFell, the Bengals didn’t take him top ten to not throw to him. Ross is a good pick late in leagues that offer big play bonuses.

While he did perform well at the end of last season and caught 32 of his 48 targets, Mitchell has to compete with a plethora of weapons on the New England offense to get touches at all. He’s barely on fantasy radar at draft time this season.

**67.** **Will Fuller V - Hou:** Fuller has broken his collarbone in training camp, and hampers his ability to improve on his 635 yard season from a year ago. While it remains to be seen how Houston’s quarterback situation will play out, Fuller was a big play receiver who also returned some kicks and punts on special teams. Take note of Fuller’s injury status before selecting him this year, but he’s worth little more than a bench spot regardles.

**68.** **Tavon Austin - LAR:** Tavon Austin caught only 58 of his 107 targets in 2016, but the Rams’ passing attack should be significantly improved this season and rejuvenated under new coach Sean McVay. Austin is sort of a jack of all trades, and tough to gauge for fantasy purposes on a weekly basis, but he is barely reliable in most formats due to his low yardage production. Wait to see how he is going to be utilized before investing too much in him.

**69.** **Allen Hurns - Jac:** Allen Hurns was a victim of touchdown regression last season, and his 477 yards on 76 targets represented a significant downturn from his previous season. Hurns now finds himself battling with Marqise Lee for targets alongside Allen Robinson, and is also relying on Blake Bortles to reliably and consistently get him the ball. Hurns is a reach in fantasy leagues this season.

**70.** **Taylor Gabriel - Atl:** Gabriel had 579 yards on only 35 receptions last season, and he really picked up toward the end of the year. He’s a big play threat in a powerful Atlanta offense, and while the passing attack as a whole should regress a bit from their dominant 2016, they are still a formidable unit. Gabriel is especially useful in big play bonus leagues, as Matthew Berry at ESPN noted that one of every seven receptions he had last season went for at least 30 yards. Gabriel is a flex play with upside, but he could be a popular pick, so don’t reach for him too high.

**71.** **Mike Williams - LAC:** Mike Williams is a highly recognized rookie who figures to be an immediate factor in the Chargers’ passing attack this season - if he is healthy. In an offense not short of options, he poses a big red zone target to help replace the aging Antonio Gates. He’s an intriguing late round pick that has both injury risk and touchdown upside.

**72.** **Devin Funchess - Car:** Funchess suffered from a struggling offense overall last season, but should rise along with the rest of the Panthers in 2017. He won’t be worth fantasy gold by any means, but his targets, receptions, and yards should all increase with Ted Ginn’s departure. Funchess is worth no more than a late round flier this year, but he should see a lot more work than last year.

He’s an intriguing PPR sleeper pick, and worth a look late in the draft.

**76.** **Nelson Agholor - Phi:** Agholor had a tough season last year, putting up less than 400 yards on 70 targets. Word out of Philly training camp is that Agholor is doing very well, and could see a lot of snaps in the slot (Jordan Matthews’ usual role). While Agholor could benefit from an uptick in targets, don’t believe media hype until you see it on the field. While Agholor can hold some deep round sleeper appeal, keep in mind that he had 0 red zone touchdowns last season on 14 targets, and caught just barely over 50% of his targets last season.

That said, he’s worth no more than a late round flier.

**_Unranked Receivers That Could Make an Impact_**

**Cooper Kupp - LAR:** Rookie Cooper Kupp was highly touted coming into this year’s NFL Draft, and the Rams bit on the hype in the third round. Kupp should step into a role where he can contribute immediately alongside Tavon Austin and Robert Woods. Known as a Julian Edelman or Wes Welker type of possession receiver, Kupp could generate flex numbers in PPR if he is offered the opportunity in the Rams’ mediocre offense.

**Tyler Boyd - Cin:** Boyd should be affected by John Ross’ drafting into the Cincinnati receiving room, but could see a reliable possession type role emerges this season. He’s worth putting on your watch list as he had 603 yards last season on 81 targets.

**Kenny Golladay - Det.** Rookie Kenny Golladay should see some immediate work in Detroit’s offense. He’ll start off behind Marvin Jones and Golden Tate, but he’s a reliable receiver that could make an impact in his first season.

**Torrey Smith - Phi.** Torrey Smith heads to the Eagles this season to join Alshon Jeffery and Jordan Matthews at receiver. He’s a deep ball threat, and thus worth a look in leagues with big play bonuses, but not much more than that.

**Braxton Miller - Hou.** Miller could benefit from Will Fuller’s broken collarbone, and should move up draft boards because of it. Keep an eye on him late in the draft.

**Brandon LaFell - Cin:** LaFell quietly put up 862 receiving yards on 106 targets last year. While John Ross and Tyler Boyd give him stiff competition, he could still be the reliable veteran presence he has been throughout his career.

**Laquon Treadwell - Min.** The most highly touted receiver of last year’s receiving class in the NFL Draft, Treadwell could see a big rise in production this year. However, Stefon Diggs and Adam Thielen have the receiving jobs in Minnesota fairly locked up.

**Josh Gordon - Cle.** Pending reinstatement, Gordon could be a WR2 or even WR1. Odds are, he won’t be reinstated. Just keep an eye on his situation throughout the season.



## **_TE:_**


**1.** **Rob Gronkowski - NE:** Gronkowski is arguably the greatest tight end of all time, and he definitely lives up to that billing in fantasy. He’s very injury prone, but gives your team a legitimate chance to win every single time he steps on the field. He is allegedly a full go in 2017, and while its not smart to reach for him too early in the draft, he should be gone by the end of the second round, and rightfully so.

| Rank  | Player Name  | Targets       | Receptions         | Receiving Yards | Receiving TD’s  | Red Zone Targets  | Red Zone Receptions  | Red Zone Receiving TD's  |
| ------------- | ------------- |:-------------:| -----:| -----:| -----:| -----:| -----:| -----:|
| **1** | **_Rob Gronkowski_** | 38   | 25 | 540 | 3 | 5 | 2 | 1 |



**2.** **Travis Kelce - KC:** Travis Kelce was the leading tight end last season, and he should see an uptick in targets with Maclin gone. The conservative Chiefs offense fed Kelce for 1,125 yards last year despite only 4 touchdowns, and Kelce again should be a focal point of the passing game in Kansas City. Look for Kelce to again be a top 5 tight end, but don’t go chasing his stats from last year as he is sure to regress a bit.

| Rank  | Player Name  | Targets       | Receptions         | Receiving Yards | Receiving TD’s  | Red Zone Targets  | Red Zone Receptions  | Red Zone Receiving TD's  |
| ------------- | ------------- |:-------------:| -----:| -----:| -----:| -----:| -----:| -----:|
| **2** | **_Travis Kelce_** | 117   | 85 | 1,125 | 4 | 16 | 8 | 3 |



**3.** **Greg Olsen - Car:** Olsen led Panthers with 129 targets last year, and is a prime candidate to do so again in 2017. Second and third in targets were Kelvin and Ted Ginn (who is off to New Orleans), and while the Panthers added two pass catching running back/wide receivers in the draft in the form of Christian McCaffrey and Curtis Samuel, Olsen should still be a top tight end in fantasy this year, and is a reliable pick as he has not missed a game since 2007.


| Rank  | Player Name  | Targets       | Receptions         | Receiving Yards | Receiving TD’s  | Red Zone Targets  | Red Zone Receptions  | Red Zone Receiving TD's  |
| ------------- | ------------- |:-------------:| -----:| -----:| -----:| -----:| -----:| -----:|
| **3** | **_Greg Olsen_** | 127   | 80 | 1,073 | 3 | 16 | 9 | 2 |



**4.** **Jordan Reed - Was:** Jordan Reed has an incredible amount of injury and concussion issues, but he is one of the best PPG players at the position. Reed has missed six games in the last two season (which doesn’t sound terrible considering how often he seems to be hurt), and is an injury risk again this season. However, the Washington offense is potent - despite losing DeSean Jackson and Pierre Garcon in free agency - and the addition of Terrelle Pryor should help alleviate some coverage pressure on Reed. Don’t reach too high for him, but he’s a great tight end to have in fantasy this year.

| Rank  | Player Name  | Targets       | Receptions         | Receiving Yards | Receiving TD’s  | Red Zone Targets  | Red Zone Receptions  | Red Zone Receiving TD's  |
| ------------- | ------------- |:-------------:| -----:| -----:| -----:| -----:| -----:| -----:|
| **4** | **_Jordan Reed_** | 87   | 66 | 686 | 6 | 12 | 8 | 5 |



**5.** **Jimmy Graham - Sea:** Graham was expected to do great things when he moved over to the Seahawks, but he was a boom or bust player last season. He may be somewhat injury prone and getting older, but still has a chance to be productive in a powerful Seattle offense. Matthew Berry at ESPN noted that Russell Wilson's passing yardage total has increased every season of his career, and Graham should again benefit this season. He quietly had 923 years last year and should come close again this year, and could be a great TE sleeper pick if he can reel in a few more of his 17 red zone targets last season for touchdowns (he had only 4). He’s a great pick at TE after the big 4.

| Rank  | Player Name  | Targets       | Receptions         | Receiving Yards | Receiving TD’s  | Red Zone Targets  | Red Zone Receptions  | Red Zone Receiving TD's  |
| ------------- | ------------- |:-------------:| -----:| -----:| -----:| -----:| -----:| -----:|
| **5** | **_Jimmy Graham_** | 95   | 65 | 923 | 6 | 17 | 6 | 4 |



**6.** **Tyler Eifert - Cin:** Eifert is a tough player to gauge the fantasy draft value of. He only played 8 games last season, but was a top level tight end in each week he played. When he is healthy, he consistently gets targets and TD opportunities (all five of his touchdowns last season came in the red zone). The addition of John Ross should help to open up opposing defenses a bit, but Eifert is way too big on an injury risk to take early on. He’s worth a fantasy selection as a TE1, but make sure you have a reliable and solid backup.

| Rank  | Player Name  | Targets       | Receptions         | Receiving Yards | Receiving TD’s  | Red Zone Targets  | Red Zone Receptions  | Red Zone Receiving TD's  |
| ------------- | ------------- |:-------------:| -----:| -----:| -----:| -----:| -----:| -----:|
| **6** | **_Tyler Eifert_** | 47   | 29 | 394 | 5 | 9 | 5 | 5 |



**7.** **Kyle Rudolph - Min:** Kyle Rudolph led all TE’s and all Vikings in targets with 132 last season, and he is a good value here again in 2017. Both offensive coordinator Pat Shurmur and head coach Mike Zimmer love to throw to TE’s, as both have over 20% of their offense’s target share going to TE’s in recent seasons, and look for Rudolph to reap the benefits of that again this season. His red zone usage is his greatest value - he was targeted 24 times from inside the 20. That usage in Minnesota’s slow and conservative offense is well worth selecting in fantasy drafts as a reliable starting tight end.

| Rank  | Player Name  | Targets       | Receptions         | Receiving Yards | Receiving TD’s  | Red Zone Targets  | Red Zone Receptions  | Red Zone Receiving TD's  |
| ------------- | ------------- |:-------------:| -----:| -----:| -----:| -----:| -----:| -----:|
| **7** | **_Kyle Rudolph_** | 132   | 83 | 840 | 7 | 24 | 14 | 5 |



**8.** **Delanie Walker - Ten:** The Titans added a ton of firepower this past offseason in the form of Eric Decker and a slew of rookies led by 5th overall pick Corey Davis. He has 333 targets in the last 3 seasons combined, showing a great usage value, and Mariota knows Walker is a reliable target. Despite the uptick in competition for targets, Walker should see enough of them this season to still be a top 10 player at the position.


| Rank  | Player Name  | Targets       | Receptions         | Receiving Yards | Receiving TD’s  | Red Zone Targets  | Red Zone Receptions  | Red Zone Receiving TD's  |
| ------------- | ------------- |:-------------:| -----:| -----:| -----:| -----:| -----:| -----:|
| **8** | **_Delanie Walker_** | 102   | 65 | 800 | 7 | 16 | 8 | 5 |



**9.** **Martellus Bennett - GB:** Bennett head up to Wisconsin this offseason to join Green Bay’s already potent passing offense. While Bennett is a great talent, Rodgers has thrown only 17.1 percent of his completions to TE’s since 2014, making Bennett’s role a bit of a scary one for fantasy purposes, but he could be the tight end that breaks that mold if he stays healthy. Bennett gives Rodgers another big target to look for in the end zone, where 5 of his 7 touchdowns came last season. Success for tight ends has been sporadic in Green Bay in recent years, and thus Bennett is merely a high upside pick due to the talent of both him and Rodgers for those who waited to take a starting TE until later in the draft.

| Rank  | Player Name  | Targets       | Receptions         | Receiving Yards | Receiving TD’s  | Red Zone Targets  | Red Zone Receptions  | Red Zone Receiving TD's  |

**10.** **Zach Ertz - Phi:** The entire fantasy world has been waiting on the Ertz breakout tour for quite some time, but the Eagles significantly upgraded the receiving corps this offseason by adding Torrey Smith and Alshon Jeffery. Ertz had 106 targets last season and 58.3 yards per game, which is behind only Kelce, Gronk, and Olsen among TE’s. He’s a sneaky good TE2 this year, with the upside to be a lower level TE1 if he can get some more TD grabs.

**11.** **Eric Ebron - Det:** Ebron averaged 55 yards per game in 2016, but only scored 1 touchdown on the entire season on 86 targets. With Anquan Boldin gone, there are 22 red zone targets from last season now up for grabs in Detroit. Ebron should (hopefully) be able to see some of those, and elevate his game to be a good TE2 and matchup based TE1 in fantasy this season.

**12.** **Hunter Henry - LAC:** Despite Hunter Henry playing second fiddle to Antonio Gates last season, he still put up 478 and 8 touchdowns on a mere 54 targets. He has a ton of target competition in LA with rookie receiver Mike Williams joining an already crowded receiving unit, and Antonio Gates still lurks on the Chargers’ roster. Henry’s potential is great this season, but he shouldn’t be reached for in drafts due to the amount of other people competing for targets from Philip Rivers. Henry is a a solid TE2 this year.

| **12** | **_Hunter Henry_** | 54   | 36 | 478 | 8 | 16 | 10 | 7 |



**13.** **Jack Doyle - Ind:** Andrew Luck’s love of tight ends is no secret. Over the last three seasons, tight ends have received 25% of Andrew Luck’s completions, 24% of passing yards, and 37% of his TD’s. Mike Clay at ESPN noted that over the past 10 years, the offenses of Colts head coach Chuck Pagano and offensive coordinator Rob Chudzinski have directed a minimum of 20 percent of the targets to the tight end position. Doyle is a popular sleeper target this season - and for good reason. He should blow by his stats from last year as Dwayne Allen is now in New England, and should be a TE1 this year.

| Rank  | Player Name  | Targets       | Receptions         | Receiving Yards | Receiving TD’s  | Red Zone Targets  | Red Zone Receptions  | Red Zone Receiving TD's  |
| ------------- | ------------- |:-------------:| -----:| -----:| -----:| -----:| -----:| -----:|
| **13** | **_Jack Doyle_** | 75   | 59 | 584 | 5 | 12 | 9 | 4 |



**14.** **Coby Fleener - NO:** Fleener was hailed as a disappointment in his first year with the Saints, but he was quietly a top 12 TE while only starting 8 games. He received 81 targets in that span, and Brandin Cooks’ departure could open more targets up. The Saints’ offense is still the best passing offense in the league - over 5,000 yards through the air last season - and Fleener should be a good bounce back candidate if he can stay healthy. He’s a quality TE2 that has some upside due to his offense in New Orleans.

| Rank  | Player Name  | Targets       | Receptions         | Receiving Yards | Receiving TD’s  | Red Zone Targets  | Red Zone Receptions  | Red Zone Receiving TD's  |
| ------------- | ------------- |:-------------:| -----:| -----:| -----:| -----:| -----:| -----:|
| **14** | **_Coby Fleener_** | 82   | 50 | 631| 3 | 16 | 9 | 2 |



**15.** **Jason Witten - Dal:** The aging Witten proved to be a reliable target for rookie Dak Prescott last year, seeing 95 targets and turning them into 673 yards. Witten also had 16 red zone targets last season, an ever important stat when it comes to fantasy tight ends. While he is bound to slow down sometime soon, he will still be relied on in a young Dallas offense, and is a decent TE2, especially in PPR leagues.


| Rank  | Player Name  | Targets       | Receptions         | Receiving Yards | Receiving TD’s  | Red Zone Targets  | Red Zone Receptions  | Red Zone Receiving TD's  |
| ------------- | ------------- |:-------------:| -----:| -----:| -----:| -----:| -----:| -----:|
| **15** | **_Jason Witten_** | 95   | 69 | 673 | 3 | 16 | 10 | 2 |



**16.** **Cameron Brate - TB:** Cameron Brate faces significant competition from sensational rookie OJ Howard for snaps at tight end, but proved to be a reliable target for Jameis Winston in 2016. Brate was tops in the NFL in yards per routes run last year, and scored 8 TD’s on 16 red zone targets last season. The other Bucs offseason addition - DeSean Jackson - should take a lot of the deeper passes away from Brate, and OJ Howard should only see his role increase as the season goes on. Brate is a low level TE2, and a risky pick this year with the impending OJ Howard Experience.

| Rank  | Player Name  | Targets       | Receptions         | Receiving Yards | Receiving TD’s  | Red Zone Targets  | Red Zone Receptions  | Red Zone Receiving TD's  |
| ------------- | ------------- |:-------------:| -----:| -----:| -----:| -----:| -----:| -----:|
| **16** | **_Cameron Brate_** | 81   | 57 | 660 | 8 | 16 | 10 | 8 |



**17.** **Julius Thomas - Mia:** Julius Thomas has been an injury prone player throughout his career, having never eclipsed 800 receiving yards in a season. He is great in the red zone - exemplified by 3 of his 4 2016 touchdowns coming from within the 20 - and is now in Miami, undoubtedly a better offense than his former Jacksonville squad. Thomas shouldn’t be relied on as even a reliable TE2, but he does have some upside by returning to an Adam Gase-led offense. He’s got late sleeper appeal.

**18.** **CJ Fiedorowicz - Hou:** Fiedorowicz will (hopefully) benefit from improved quarterback play this season, but that remains to be seen until the first few games of the season. Fiedorowicz saw 89 targets last season (top 10 for TE),  and12 of those were in red zone (more than AJ Green, Julio, B. Cooks). Don’t count on him to carry your fantasy team through the season, but he’s a low end TE2 in a new look offense that could feature him heavily.

**19.** **Austin Hooper - Atl:** Hooper is now the starting tight end in Georgia after having a good season last year, and should see highly increased targets because of it. Atlanta has one of the league’s best offenses, and Hooper could benefit greatly from being the sole tight end this season. He’s a great high-upside pick in this year’s fantasy drafts, and worth a late round look.

**20.** **Antonio Gates - LAC:** The future Hall of Fame saw 18 red zone targets last season (top 12 in all of the NFL) despite seeing less than 100 total targets. Gates will undoubtedly lose time to second year TE Hunter Henry, and target competition from the large group of LAC wide receivers also brings his fantasy value down. Gates is a touchdown or bust player this year, and is a tough, low upside choice in fantasy drafts.

**21.** **OJ Howard - TB:** While rookie tight ends are usually never on the fantasy radar, OJ Howard is a special enough talent to warrant fantasy interest. He is a huge target that can fly (4.51 40 yard dash), and joins a powerful offense where opposing defenses already need to account for Mike Evans and other offseason acquisition DeSean Jackson. Howard could step into a solid role faster than any of us realize, and is well worth a late round selection in fantasy squads for upside alone.

**22.** **David Njoku - Cle:** Another high upside rookie, first round selection David Njoku comes into an immediate role in Cleveland with only second year player Seth DeValve standing in his way. While he shouldn’t be counted on as a reliable fantasy asset, he is a talented receiver and could be set up for a decent role as a rookie in what should be an improved Cleveland offense. He is worth taking a late round look.

**23.** **Jared Cook - Oak:** Jared Cook had 32 targets in GB’s 3 playoff games last season for 230 and 2 TD’s, a good image of what he can do when given opportunities. In Oakland, he gives Carr and Co. a good receiving option at tight end, but should face target competition from incumbent Clive Walford. He’s got some upside, but is best left for leagues that start 2 TE’s.

**24.** **Zach Miller - Chi:** Zach Miller missed 6 games last season, and the Bears drafted rookie Adam Shaheen in the NFL Draft this past April. Glennon will need someone to throw to, and surely the tight end position is in the mix for targets in an offense that will often be playing catch-up later in games. He could get a decent volume of work this season, but he’s merely a fantasy backup this year.

**25.** **Evan Engram - NYG:** Evan Engram is another rookie tight end that could make a splash this season despite the knowledge that the position usually takes time to develop into the NFL game. Engram is a solid receiver already - essentially a slot receiver - and should get some looks despite the presence of Odell Beckham, Sterling Shepard, and newcomer Brandon Marshall. Mike Clay at ESPN noted that during each of coach Ben McAdoo's three seasons with the Giants, at least 19 percent of the team's targets have gone to the tight end. That number should stand pat, if not go up, with a talent like Engram. He could be a solid backup tight end when the season is all said and done.

**26.** **Jesse James - Pit:** Jesse James assumes the Heath Miller-esque tight end role in Pittsburgh that had been known for sporadic target shares until the end zone is within reach. While tight ends and touchdowns go hand in hand for fantasy relevance and significant, James has too many weapons around him competing for targets to be a true threat in fantasy leagues. He could be a nice backup, but don’t rely on James to carry you through the season.

**27.** **Dwayne Allen - NE:** This year’s Martellus Bennett, Dwayne Allen comes to the Patriots to join Rob Gronkowski in the tight ends room. Allen was a top 10 TE last year despite injuries, and Gronk has injury risk himself. Allen has high upside when he is healthy, and is a unique TE handcuff for Gronk and could potentially be a worthy backup in his own right. Keep in mind that Martellus Bennett was top 10 fantasy TE last season from weeks 14-16 when Gronk was hurt.

**28.** **Charles Clay - Buf:** - Charles Clay put up 552 yards last season on 87 targets, and shouldn’t be counted on for much more this season. While the Buffalo offense will surely throw more with Rex Ryan out of the picture, Clay isn’t known for big plays and is fairly reliant (like most tight ends) on the touchdown to stay fantasy relevant. He’s best left to leagues that start 2 tight ends.

**29.** **Vernon Davis - Was:** Davis is valuable as a backup to Jordan Reed in an effective Redskins’ offense, as he put up over 580 yards last season on only 59 targets. He’s worth a late round look in deeper leagues if you need a TE, especially if you have Reed.

**30.** **Tyler Higbee - LAR:** Higbee avoided jail time from his altercation last year, and should play a decent role in the Rams new look offense in 2017. He’s a big and fast target capable of creating severe mismatches, but it remains to be seen how he’ll be utilized and how the Rams offense as a whole can produce. He’s a late round sleeper in fantasy leagues.

He’s shown potential before, and is worth a bench spot (or as high as a TE2 in PPR leagues) in drafts this year due to Baltimore’s pass heavy offense.

## **_K:_**

**1.** **Stephen Gostkowski - NE:** While the Patriots offense was again elite in NFL terms, Gostkowski did not exactly perform as many would have guessed in fantasy terms. With only 4 attempts of 50 or more yards (and 32 attempts total), his 49 extra point attempts carried him through the season as a reliable kicker as the weeks wound down. That said, the Patriots offense should be even more powerful this season with the additions of Brandin Cooks and Dwayne Allen, and Gostkowski might not be the first kicker off the board as he has been in years past. He’s as close as you’ll ever find to a ‘sleeper’ candidate at the kicker position, but don’t reach for kickers!

| Rank  | Player Name  | FG Made/FG Attempted      | 50+ Yard FG Made/50+ Yard FG Attempted | XP Made/XP Attempted  |
| ------------- | ------------- |:-------------:|:-------------:|:-------------:|
| **1** | **_Stephen Gostkowski_** | 27/32   | 2/4 | 46/49 |


**2.** **Justin Tucker - Bal:** Justin Tucker was a dominant kicker in 2016, and his fantasy output exemplified that perfectly. He missed only one field goal on the entire season and also nailed all of his 27 extra point attempts. He had 10 field goal attempts from over 50 yards and made all ten of them, a significant stat from a fantasy standpoint. While the Ravens’ pedestrian offense (T-23rd in red zone attempts per game last season) hinders Tucker’s total point output a bit, they should improve this season. Tucker’s ability to hit 50+ yard kicks with consistency propels him to the top of the kicker draft board.

| Rank  | Player Name  | FG Made/FG Attempted      | 50+ Yard FG Made/50+ Yard FG Attempted | XP Made/XP Attempted  |
| ------------- | ------------- |:-------------:|:-------------:|:-------------:|
| **2** | **_Justin Tucker_** | 38/39   | 10/10 | 27/27 |



**3.** **Dan Bailey - Dal:** Dan Bailey is one of the most accurate kickers in history, and should again prove why this season. The Cowboys were on a roll the entire regular season last year, and Bailey was perfect on all 46 of his extra point attempts to help carry him through fantasy games. He was only 27 of 32 on field goals last season and made only 2 of his 6 attempts that were 50 or more yards, but he has a high floor as an accurate kicker on a good offense in a kicker-friendly stadium. Bailey is a reliable investment for fantasy purposes, but don’t expect him to carry your team to victory. He’s a high floor – low ceiling type of kicker in fantasy.

| Rank  | Player Name  | FG Made/FG Attempted      | 50+ Yard FG Made/50+ Yard FG Attempted | XP Made/XP Attempted  |
| ------------- | ------------- |:-------------:|:-------------:|:-------------:|
| **3** | **_Dan Bailey_** | 27/32   | 3/6 | 46/46 |



**4.** **Matt Bryant - Atl:** Playing in a dome week in and week out, Matt Bryant was a prime fantasy beneficiary of the Falcons’ juggernaut offense in 2016. He made 56 of his 57 extra point attempts – which is astounding in itself – and was also good for 34 of 37 field goal tries. Opportunity and distance consistency are the two best predictors of kicker success in fantasy, and Bryant has them both, as he was 6-8 from 50 or more yards last season in addition to his high kicking percentages. The Atlanta offense should regress a bit this season, especially with offensive coordinator Kyle Shanahan moving onto San Francisco, but Bryant should again find himself in a reliable position as a top level fantasy kicker.

| Rank  | Player Name  | FG Made/FG Attempted      | 50+ Yard FG Made/50+ Yard FG Attempted | XP Made/XP Attempted  |
| ------------- | ------------- |:-------------:|:-------------:|:-------------:|
| **4** | **_Matt Bryant_** | 34/37   | 6/8 | 56/57 |



**5.** **Mason Crosby - GB:** Mason Crosby is a talented kicker in his own right, but his home field and lack of field goal volume drop him a bit in preseason fantasy rankings. He attempted only 30 total field goals last season, and only 2 of 50 or more yards. He has a tough job playing in the tundra of Lambeau Field – especially later in the season – but does have one of the top offenses in the NFL to get him into scoring position. Unfortunately for Crosby – and those who drafted him in fantasy last year – those scoring positions turned into 47 extra points instead of more field goals. Regardless, Crosby is a solid kicker to take if you’re one of the last in your league to grab one.

| Rank  | Player Name  | FG Made/FG Attempted      | 50+ Yard FG Made/50+ Yard FG Attempted | XP Made/XP Attempted  |
| ------------- | ------------- |:-------------:|:-------------:|:-------------:|
| **5** | **_Mason Crosby_** | 26/30   | 1/2 | 44/47 |



**6.** **Adam Vinatieri - Ind:** The ageless Adam Vinatieri was in a similar spot as Gostkowski last season, in a good offense that was scoring touchdowns more than providing him field goal opportunities. He had 44 extra point attempts and only 31 total field goal attempts, but he does play in a dome (huge bonus) and benefits from a talented Indianapolis offense that averaged 3.3 red zone scoring chances per game last season. Due to both opportunity and a favorable home playing situation, Vinatieri is a solid (and, perhaps most importantly, reliable) kicker for your fantasy team.

| Rank  | Player Name  | FG Made/FG Attempted      | 50+ Yard FG Made/50+ Yard FG Attempted | XP Made/XP Attempted  |
| ------------- | ------------- |:-------------:|:-------------:|:-------------:|
| **6** | **_Adam Vinatieri_** | 27/31   | 7/9 | 44/44 |



**7.** **Cairo Santos - KC:** Santos benefits from a conservative Andy Reid attack that put him in position for 35 field goal tries and 39 extra point attempts last season. He was 8-9 on attempts over 40 yards, but only had two kicks of 50 plus yards last year. That said, the Chiefs have a good defense and solid offense that is sure to get Santos the most valuable stat when it comes to kickers in fantasy – opportunity. While weather can be unreliable down the stretch (i.e. in fantasy playoffs) in Kansas City, Santos remains a reliable fantasy kicker for your squad.

| Rank  | Player Name  | FG Made/FG Attempted      | 50+ Yard FG Made/50+ Yard FG Attempted | XP Made/XP Attempted  |
| ------------- | ------------- |:-------------:|:-------------:|:-------------:|
| **7** | **_Cairo Santos_** | 31/35   | 2/2 | 36/39 |



**8.** **Matt Prater - Det:** Matt Prater of the Detroit Lions is a very undervalued fantasy kicker. While he is a boom or bust type of player at the kicker position (somehow), his home stadium, team, and leg power boost him to fantasy relevance on a weekly basis. He was 24 of 29 from within 49 yards last season, but Prater nailed all 7 of his attempts last season of 50 or more yards, has a good offense run by Matthew Stafford to get him into scoring positions, and plays in a dome for at least 8 games per season. If you’re looking for a high ceiling play at kicker and willing to risk a down week every once in a while, Prater could be your guy.

| Rank  | Player Name  | FG Made/FG Attempted      | 50+ Yard FG Made/50+ Yard FG Attempted | XP Made/XP Attempted  |
| ------------- | ------------- |:-------------:|:-------------:|:-------------:|
| **8** | **_Matt Prater_** | 31/36   | 7/7 | 31/33 |



**9.** **Sebastian Janikowski - Oak:** Janikowski has been a popular fantasy kicker for some time, but his trademark deep ball has not been as effective as it was in his prime. He made only 3 of his 8 attempts from beyond 50 yards in 2016, but did hit 10 of 11 kicks from 40-49 yards. A top level Raiders offense is something Janikowski has never had the benefit of, so his attempts on both field goals and extra points will be substantial enough for him to warrant a spot as a back end starter or top level streaming option at kicker this season.

| Rank  | Player Name  | FG Made/FG Attempted      | 50+ Yard FG Made/50+ Yard FG Attempted | XP Made/XP Attempted  |
| ------------- | ------------- |:-------------:|:-------------:|:-------------:|
| **9** | **_Sebastian Janikowski_** | 29/35   | 3/8 | 37/39 |



**10.** **Wil Lutz - NO:** Lutz benefits from playing in a dome and with one of the NFL’s best offenses in New Orleans. He had a whopping 50 extra point attempts last year (making 49 of them), and also added in 34 field goals. It’s illogical to predict a repeat of those stats this year, but the Saints’ powerful offense and favorable kicking conditions on a consistent basis keep Lutz relevant as a back end starter at the kicker position.  

| Rank  | Player Name  | FG Made/FG Attempted      | 50+ Yard FG Made/50+ Yard FG Attempted | XP Made/XP Attempted  |
| ------------- | ------------- |:-------------:|:-------------:|:-------------:|
| **10** | **_Wil Lutz_** | 28/34   | 3/7 | 49/50 |



**11.** **Dustin Hopkins - Was:** As the kicker for a potent Washington offense, Hopkins had an incredible 42 attempts last season to go along with his 39 extra point attempts. He wasn’t very consistent in his league leading 42 attempts, and nailed only 3 of his 7 attempts from 50 or more yards. With Washington’s offense again in a good position to get scoring opportunities (3.8 red zone scoring attempts last season, 6th in the NFL), Hopkins is a lower end fantasy starter at the kicker position. Expect some misses and frustrating weeks, though.

| Rank  | Player Name  | FG Made/FG Attempted      | 50+ Yard FG Made/50+ Yard FG Attempted | XP Made/XP Attempted  |
| ------------- | ------------- |:-------------:|:-------------:|:-------------:|
