**12.** **Steven Hauschka - Buf:** Hauschka comes to Buffalo after a few seasons in Seattle, where he made 33 of his 37 attempts last season. While the Buffalo offense should improve a bit with defensive-minded Rex Ryan out of the picture, it’s not too reliable (especially later in the season when the weather gets worse) Hauschka’s stats will benefit all that much. He’s a streaming option at kicker this year.

| Rank  | Player Name  | FG Made/FG Attempted      | 50+ Yard FG Made/50+ Yard FG Attempted | XP Made/XP Attempted  |
| ------------- | ------------- |:-------------:|:-------------:|:-------------:|
| **12** | **_Steven Hauschka_** | 33/37   | 1/1 | 29/35 |



**13.** **Brandon McManus - Den:** McManus benefits from the mile high air in Denver and the unique ability to kick for extra distance in 8 of his 16 games each season. That said, he was only 3 of 6 on 50+ yard attempts last year. He’s got a mediocre offense leading him down the field, but perhaps that’s just what he needs some weeks to get him multiple field goal tries. He’s worth a shot in a 12 team league.

| Rank  | Player Name  | FG Made/FG Attempted      | 50+ Yard FG Made/50+ Yard FG Attempted | XP Made/XP Attempted  |
| ------------- | ------------- |:-------------:|:-------------:|:-------------:|
| **13** | **_Brandon McManus_** | 29/34   | 3/6 | 32/33 |



**14.** **Graham Gano - Car:** Gano missed 8 of his 38 kicks last year in a sputtering Carolina offense, but should improve (along with the team as a whole) in 2017. He’s been fairly reliable throughout his career, but that’s not enough to warrant draft day consideration in fantasy. There are options with greater upside here.

| Rank  | Player Name  | FG Made/FG Attempted      | 50+ Yard FG Made/50+ Yard FG Attempted | XP Made/XP Attempted  |
| ------------- | ------------- |:-------------:|:-------------:|:-------------:|
| **14** | **_Graham Gano_** | 30/38   | 3/6 | 31/34 |



**15.** **Chris Boswell - Pit:** Pittsburgh’s kicker faces tough weather and defenses for a decent amount of the season, but the powerful Steelers offense gives Boswell a boost for fantasy relevance. He hit all 36 of his extra point attempts last season, but was just 21 of 25 on his field goal attempts. That number would need to rise for Boswell to become a starting fantasy kicker, but he’s a decent matchup-based streaming option.

| Rank  | Player Name  | FG Made/FG Attempted      | 50+ Yard FG Made/50+ Yard FG Attempted | XP Made/XP Attempted  |
| ------------- | ------------- |:-------------:|:-------------:|:-------------:|
| **15** | **_Chris Boswell_** | 21/25   | 0/2 | 36/36 |



**16.** **Blair Walsh - Sea:** After a tough ending to his tenure in Minnesota, Walsh comes to Seattle to kick for a better offense than he’s ever had the pleasure of dealing with. Aside from the chip shot whiff in the playoffs and subsequent struggles, Walsh has been a decent kicker for most of his career and should do fairly well in a potent Seattle offense that averaged 3.8 red zone scoring opportunities per game in 2016 (8th in the league). Walsh is a streaming option until he can prove consistent success in rainy Seattle.

| Rank  | Player Name  | FG Made/FG Attempted      | 50+ Yard FG Made/50+ Yard FG Attempted | XP Made/XP Attempted  |
| ------------- | ------------- |:-------------:|:-------------:|:-------------:|
| **16** | **_Blair Walsh_** | 12/16   | 1/2 | 15/19 |



**17.** **Caleb Sturgis - Phi:** Sturgis was right behind Hopkins with 41 field goal attempts last season, and did a decent job with such high volume. The Eagles’ offense should be better this season as Carson Wentz adjusts to the NFL – especially with new additions Alshon Jeffery, Torrey Smith, and LeGarrette Blount – but it’s tough to say whether Sturgis will benefit or falter from this. The Eagles offense will keep Sturgis fantasy relevant in 2017, but perhaps as a streaming play unless the field goal volume stays pat from last season.

| Rank  | Player Name  | FG Made/FG Attempted      | 50+ Yard FG Made/50+ Yard FG Attempted | XP Made/XP Attempted  |
| ------------- | ------------- |:-------------:|:-------------:|:-------------:|
| **17** | **_Caleb Sturgis_** | 35/41   | 4/6 | 30/31 |



**18.** **Josh Lambo - LAC:** The Chargers’ offense added rookie receiver Mike Williams to an already crowded room, and the offense could be a real talent this year with Keenan Allen returning from injury. Lambo could see more than the 32 field goal attempts last year, but he’ll have to improve on his 0 for 3 record on kicks of 50 or more yards last season to be fantasy relevant.

| Rank  | Player Name  | FG Made/FG Attempted      | 50+ Yard FG Made/50+ Yard FG Attempted | XP Made/XP Attempted  |
| ------------- | ------------- |:-------------:|:-------------:|:-------------:|
| **18** | **_Josh Lambo_** | 26/32   | 0/3 | 42/46 |



**19.** **Nick Novak - Hou:** Nick Novak’s fantasy value comes from having a kicker friendly stadium in Houston, a dominant defense that can keep opponents off of the field for too long, and an offense that’s not quite good enough to consistently get touchdowns. Regardless of whether Tom Savage or DeShaun Watson is under center this season in Houston, Novak’s stats should be boosted up because of it. He’s a top level streaming option, if not a low-end fantasy starter.

**20.** **Chandler Catanzaro - NYJ:** Catanzaro could benefit from a mediocre Jets offense that will struggle to get past the opponents’ 20 yards line on a weekly basis, but that’s a tough thing to rely on for fantasy football purposes. Keep him out of reach on draft day.

**21.** **Phil Dawson - Ari:** Ol’ reliable Phil Dawson is still kicking in Arizona, and while his leg power has decreased in recent seasons, he’s still as accurate as they come. He’s still not worth real fantasy consideration, though.

| ------------- | ------------- |:-------------:|:-------------:|:-------------:|
| **21** | **_Phil Dawson_** | 18/21   | 1/2 | 33/34 |


## **_D/ST:_**

**1.** **Denver Broncos D/ST:** The Broncos return the majority of their top level defense this season, and should remain in that tier throughout this one. They forced 27 turnovers and were tied for 3rd in sacks, while allowing only 316.1 yards against per game in 2016 (4th best in the NFL). While it is foolish to use last year’s stats as a predictor for team defense, the Broncos defense has been so consistent the past few years that they can be trusted as again being one of the top fantasy defenses this season. Don’t reach for defenses (take them late!), but if the Broncos happen to still be there after a handful of D/ST’s have gone, might as well scoop them up. Keep in mind, however, that they do have a tough Week 15 and 16 schedule in facing Indianapolis and Washington, in addition to the [toughest strength of schedule in the NFL this season](http://www.espn.com/blog/nflnation/post/_/id/234722/2017-nfl-strength-of-schedule).

| Rank  | Player Name  | Yards Against/Game (2016)      | Points Against/Game (2016)         | Sacks | Fumbles Recovered/Fumbles Forced  | Interceptions | Defensive TD’s  | Special Teams TD's  |
| ------------- | ------------- |:-------------:| -----:| -----:| -----:| -----:| -----:| -----:|
| **1** | **_Denver Broncos D/ST_** | 316.1   | 18.6 | 42 | 13/16 | 14 | 4 | 0 |



**2.** **Seattle Seahawks D/ST:** The Seahawks underperformed - by their recent standards - but still allowed the 5th least amount of yards per game last year at 318.7. They had a whopping 42 sacks (T-3rd), and didn’t really lose anyone of note in the offseason. Their 2017 opponents had a combined winning percentage of .455 (T-25th), giving them one of the NFL’s easier schedules, and they have two winnable games in the Jaguars and Rams in Weeks 14 and 15. They do have a tough Dallas offense in Week 16, but expect Seattle’s D/ST to be at least good enough to give you a shot to get there in your fantasy league. Expect another strong season in the Pacific Northwest.

| Rank  | Player Name  | Yards Against/Game (2016)      | Points Against/Game (2016)         | Sacks | Fumbles Recovered/Fumbles Forced  | Interceptions | Defensive TD’s  | Special Teams TD's  |
| ------------- | ------------- |:-------------:| -----:| -----:| -----:| -----:| -----:| -----:|
| **2** | **_Seattle Seahawks D/ST_** | 318.7   | 18.3 | 42 | 8/16 | 11 | 1 | 0 |




**3.** **Kansas City Chiefs D/ST:** The Chiefs are notable for having a rowdy and difficult stadium to play in for opposing teams, but are also notable for having dynamic return man Tyreek Hill. Hill is a threat every time he touches the ball, and is one of the few special teams guys that gives a legitimate boost to a D/ST for fantasy purposes. In addition to Hill, the Chiefs defense scored 5 touchdowns last season themselves, and is populated with talent throughout from veterans like Tamba Hali to young up and comers like Dee Ford. Don’t rely on last year’s touchdowns to repeat (defensively, at least), but they had 33 forced turnovers last season to go along with 28 sacks. The sacks should increase if the unit remains at full health, but the Chiefs D/ST are a reliable bet to put up top ten numbers throughout the season regardless.

| Rank  | Player Name  | Yards Against/Game (2016)      | Points Against/Game (2016)         | Sacks | Fumbles Recovered/Fumbles Forced  | Interceptions | Defensive TD’s  | Special Teams TD's  |
| ------------- | ------------- |:-------------:| -----:| -----:| -----:| -----:| -----:| -----:|
| **3** | **_Kansas City Chiefs D/ST_** | 368.5   | 19.4 | 28 | 15/16 | 18 | 5 | 3 |



**4.** **Houston Texans D/ST:** JJ Watt’s impending return should help to boost the Texans defense this season, but the loss of emerging corner AJ Bouye could hurt more than the Texans realize. Rookie linebacker Zach Cunningham was a great pick in the draft who could step in and play early on the defense that allowed the least yards per game in the NFL last season. Their points against per game should improve, as the offense should (hopefully) be more effective than last year and not be giving opposing offenses good field position on a weekly basis, but the Texans are a formidable unit even without breakout corner AJ Bouye. Look for JJ Watt and Co. to have another strong fantasy finish this year, especially as they have one of the easier schedules in the league this year (T-27th).


| Rank  | Player Name  | Yards Against/Game (2016)      | Points Against/Game (2016)         | Sacks | Fumbles Recovered/Fumbles Forced  | Interceptions | Defensive TD’s  | Special Teams TD's  |
| ------------- | ------------- |:-------------:| -----:| -----:| -----:| -----:| -----:| -----:|
| **4** | **_Houston Texans D/ST_** | 301.3   | 20.5 | 31 | 6/7 | 11 | 1 | 1 |



**5.** **Minnesota Vikings D/ST:** The Vikings had a superb 7 touchdowns from their D/ST last season, with 3 coming via special teams. Cordarrelle Patterson’s departure to Oakland hurts that potential a bit, but the defense itself is loaded with talent. The line had 41 sacks last season (5th) and had 27 forced turnovers to add. While the Vikings conservative offense does a good job of holding onto the ball and keeping the defense off the field (12th most time of possession in 2016), the defense does its own job of keeping opposing teams at bay. The Vikings won’t be a sexy pick in drafts this year, but they should be a very effective one.

| Rank  | Player Name  | Yards Against/Game (2016)      | Points Against/Game (2016)         | Sacks | Fumbles Recovered/Fumbles Forced  | Interceptions | Defensive TD’s  | Special Teams TD's  |
| ------------- | ------------- |:-------------:| -----:| -----:| -----:| -----:| -----:| -----:|
| **5** | **_Minnesota Vikings D/ST_** | 314.9   | 19.2 | 41 | 13/13 | 14 | 4 | 3 |



**6.** **Arizona Cardinals D/ST:** Arizona’s defense gave up only 305.2 yards per game last season, second in the NFL to only the Houston Texans. Add in their league leading 48 sacks, their 14 fumble recoveries (2nd in the NFL), and their 14 interceptions (T-12th), and it is easy to see why the Cardinals have been a reliable D/ST unit for the last few seasons. Patrick Peterson provides them with a shutdown corner that can match up with any receiver in the NFL, and rookie Haasan Reddick could be a wildcard for the Arizona defense this season after his highly productive season at Temple University. The Cardinals once again bring a top level defense to the board, and could be one of the elite groups by the end of the season. Take them with confidence.

| Rank  | Player Name  | Yards Against/Game (2016)      | Points Against/Game (2016)         | Sacks | Fumbles Recovered/Fumbles Forced  | Interceptions | Defensive TD’s  | Special Teams TD's  |
| ------------- | ------------- |:-------------:| -----:| -----:| -----:| -----:| -----:| -----:|
| **6** | **_Arizona Cardinals D/ST_** | 305.2   | 22.6 | 48 | 14/21 | 14 | 3 | 0 |



**7.** **New England Patriots D/ST:** One of the most under the radar fantasy defenses, the New England Patriots benefit from good coaching and schemes, an offense that kept the ball for an average time of 31:18 each game last season (4th), and a quality group of players that combined for 34 sacks and 23 takeaways last season. The Patriots should again be a top team in the league - with talk of them going 19-0 floating around the media - and their D/ST group should be a top fantasy asset yet again. They are a great pick to lead your team to success, and should be available later than a lot of other top defenses.

| Rank  | Player Name  | Yards Against/Game (2016)      | Points Against/Game (2016)         | Sacks | Fumbles Recovered/Fumbles Forced  | Interceptions | Defensive TD’s  | Special Teams TD's  |
| ------------- | ------------- |:-------------:| -----:| -----:| -----:| -----:| -----:| -----:|
| **7** | **_New England Patriots D/ST_** | 326.4   | 15.6 | 34 | 10/16 | 13 | 0 | 0 |



**8.** **Carolina Panthers D/ST:** The Carolina Panthers added Captain Munnerlyn, Mike Adams, and Julius Peppers this offseason in an effort to return to their 2015 form when they went to the Super Bowl. They were second in the NFL last season with 47 sacks, but regressed in many other departments last season. While they could be due for improvement this season, their division has improved greatly and they have a tough few games in Weeks 15 and 16 against Green Bay and Tampa Bay. They will get you through the season alright, but don’t rely on the Panthers as your sole D/ST this year. Make sure you have another quality (top-15) unit on your squad.

| Rank  | Player Name  | Yards Against/Game (2016)      | Points Against/Game (2016)         | Sacks | Fumbles Recovered/Fumbles Forced  | Interceptions | Defensive TD’s  | Special Teams TD's  |
| ------------- | ------------- |:-------------:| -----:| -----:| -----:| -----:| -----:| -----:|
| **8** | **_Carolina Panthers D/ST_** | 359.8   | 25.1 | 47 | 10/18 | 17 | 3 | 0 |



**9.** **New York Giants D/ST:** The Giants were a surprise D/ST unit last year in the fantasy world, and the emergence of Landon Collins as one of the NFL’s best safeties has given this group a formidable secondary to build around. The Giants should have their hands full with their division and during the fantasy playoffs, with games against Dallas, Philadelphia, and Arizona on tap for Weeks 14-16. They are in a similar boat as the Panthers in that they are a good unit to own, but make sure you have at least one other quality unit on your roster.


| Rank  | Player Name  | Yards Against/Game (2016)      | Points Against/Game (2016)         | Sacks | Fumbles Recovered/Fumbles Forced  | Interceptions | Defensive TD’s  | Special Teams TD's  |
| ------------- | ------------- |:-------------:| -----:| -----:| -----:| -----:| -----:| -----:|
| **9** | **_New York Giants D/ST_** | 339.7   | 17.8 | 35 | 8/15 | 17 | 4 | 0 |



**10.** **Jacksonville Jaguars D/ST:** It seems like we have been waiting forever for the Jaguars defense to finally break out, but this may actually be the year. While they only had 13 turnovers on the season, they were 6th best in yards allowed per game, and added veterans Calais Campbell and Barry Church as well as breakout corner AJ Bouye. With the [second easiest strength of schedule in the NFL this season](http://www.espn.com/blog/nflnation/post/_/id/234722/2017-nfl-strength-of-schedule), the Jaguars could be an epic sleeper pick if all their finely gathered pieces come together. They also draw the 49ers in Week 16. The Jags are a sleeper pick and quality D/ST2 in nearly any format.

| Rank  | Player Name  | Yards Against/Game (2016)      | Points Against/Game (2016)         | Sacks | Fumbles Recovered/Fumbles Forced  | Interceptions | Defensive TD’s  | Special Teams TD's  |
| ------------- | ------------- |:-------------:| -----:| -----:| -----:| -----:| -----:| -----:|
| **10** | **_Jacksonville Jaguars D/ST_** | 321.7   | 25 | 33 | 6/10 | 7 | 1 | 1 |



**11.** **Los Angeles Rams D/ST:** The Rams as a whole were a mess last season. While coach Jeff Fisher is out and the Rams have a whole new look, they did lose TJ McDonald this offseason. Connor Barwin might have been their best defensive addition, but that may speak for itself. The Rams are a group that has talent (think Aaron Donald) but minimal upside, as the team as a whole leaves a lot to be desired. They’re a solid group, and are settled in as a D/ST2 this season.

| ------------- | ------------- |:-------------:| -----:| -----:| -----:| -----:| -----:| -----:|
| **11** | **_Los Angeles Rams D/ST_** | 337   | 24.6 | 31 | 8/12 | 10 | 1 | 0 |



**12.** **Baltimore Ravens D/ST:** The Ravens defense will benefit from the [9th easiest schedule this season by last year’s strength of schedule metric](http://www.espn.com/blog/nflnation/post/_/id/234722/2017-nfl-strength-of-schedule), but are a good unit in their own right. They finished in the top ten in both yards allowed and points allowed last season, and they could do the same this year behind CJ Mosley and company. The addition of Tony Jefferson adds a significant element to their secondary not seen since Ed Reed retired. Expect Baltimore to be a good value on draft day, and worth your pick if you’re one of the last teams to grab a defense.

**13.** **Philadelphia Eagles D/ST:** The Eagles upgraded their defensive line in the first round of the draft by adding Derek Barnett, and also acquired Chris Long and Timmy Jernigan to shore up the front seven. This group should improve on the 34 sacks the Birds had last year, and although the secondary is scary weak, the Eagles should be talented enough on both sides of the ball to keep their opponents at bay throughout a majority of the season. The Eagles are a great defense to use in a tandem with another unit, as they have a relatively tough schedule this year but face the Rams in Week 14 (week one of fantasy playoffs). They’re a great value down this low.

**14.** **Pittsburgh Steelers D/ST:** The Pittsburgh defense was average on many accounts last season, and lost veteran Lawrence Timmons in the offseason. The Steelers did add linebacker TJ Watt in the NFL Draft, and has a potent offense to help in securing and holding onto leads in many games, but the Pittsburgh unit has some vulnerabilities that could be exploited by good offenses. That said, they boast the league’s [5th easiest schedule in the NFL this season](http://www.espn.com/blog/nflnation/post/_/id/234722/2017-nfl-strength-of-schedule), but face New England in Week 15. The Steelers D/ST is low upside this season, but still not a bad backup.

**15.** **Cincinnati Bengals D/ST:** The Bengals are a talented defense, averaging only 19.7 points against per game last year (8th) and posting a respectable 33 sacks while also nabbing 17th interceptions on the season (T-4th). While the Bengals play in a historically tough AFC North, they have the [4th easiest schedule in the NFL this season](http://www.espn.com/blog/nflnation/post/_/id/234722/2017-nfl-strength-of-schedule), and could be a great value pick. They are a great sleeper and backup this season, and get Bears-Vikings-Lions in Weeks 14-16. Could be much, much worse.

**16.** **Green Bay Packers D/ST:** The Packers defense was an odd fantasy play last season, allowing over 24 points against per game while generating 40 sacks and 25 total turnovers. The Packers benefit from having a world class quarterback in Aaron Rodgers and an offense to go with it, and the defense should improve from last season, but the Packers shouldn’t be relied on to carry your team through a fantasy season. They’re a backup defense this year, but you may want to snag them midway through the season if you are in the playoff hunt. Their final three games are Browns-Panthers-Vikings, offering two very favorable matchups during the fantasy playoffs. They could be a good stash.

**17.** **Los Angeles Chargers D/ST:** Joey Bosa dominated the NFL in his rookie year and is the new face of a relocated Chargers defense that is looking to make its mark. Despite posting mediocre numbers in both points and yards allowed, they did tie for the league lead with 18 interceptions. Turnovers give opportunity for the unpredictable defensive touchdown, and this unit could be a nice sleeper pick among the later defenses to be selected on the season. They’re among the higher-upside backup defenses to own.

**18.** **Oakland Raiders D/ST:** The Raiders are in the middle of a well publicized turnaround, but their offense seems to have been the major catalyst to that success. With over 24 points allowed per game last season and a mere 25 total sacks (dead last in the league), the Raiders need to improve as a whole in order to make that next step. The biggest news here for fantasy purposes is the addition of Cordarrelle Patterson, who has scored 5 kickoff return touchdowns in his 4 year career. The Raiders could fall do to their poor performance last year, but they’re worth a flier as a solid backup defense. Don’t expect top level numbers, however.

**19.** **Tampa Bay Buccaneers D/ST:** The Buccaneers upgraded their offense significantly this offseason, but failed to improve much on their middle of the road defense. They could be a decent backup defense this season due to their improvement as a team overall, but don’t expect a repeat of their 4 defensive touchdowns. The Bucs are a mid-road defensive backup this year.

**20.** **Atlanta Falcons D/ST:** The Falcons defense may have been mediocre last season, but they are an up and coming group that should improve vastly this year. Dontari Poe was a big addition to the middle of the offensive line, but the Falcons have a tough Saints-Buccaneers-Saints schedule during the fantasy playoffs. The vulnerability in crucial situations and average performance across the board leaves the Falcons best served as a backup defense this year, regardless of the widespread talent across the defensive depth chart on paper.

**21.** **Miami Dolphins D/ST:** The Miami defense added Lawrence Timmons and William Hayes this offseason, but still doesn’t pose a major threat to opposing offenses. Allowing over 380 yards per game last season the Dolphins need to improve this year to be relevant in a fantasy sense. Their 25 forced turnovers and 33 sacks are not exactly dominant, and the Dolphins have the [sixth hardest schedule this season according to last year’s winning percentage](http://www.espn.com/blog/nflnation/post/_/id/234722/2017-nfl-strength-of-schedule). Consider them barely a backup squad to start the season off for your fantasy team.

**22.** **Buffalo Bills D/ST:** The Bills lost a lot of defensive assets last season, with Zach Brown and Stephon Gilmore headlining the departing group. Coach Rex Ryan is also gone, and the defense will (presumably) be learning an entirely new system this year. They are a risky pick to repeat on their 39 sacks last season, and may be best left as a streaming option.

**23.** **Tennessee Titans D/ST:** The Titans made a splash in acquiring Jonathan Cyprien and Logan Ryan to help in the secondary, but their defense as a whole still leaves much to be desired. While they benefit from the [second easiest schedule in the NFL this season](http://www.espn.com/blog/nflnation/post/_/id/234722/2017-nfl-strength-of-schedule) from playing in the weaker AFC South, the Titans’ improved offense could be another catalyst to their potential 2017 success. They are also a sneaky good defense to have during fantasy playoffs, as they draw the 49ers and Rams in Weeks 15 and 16.

**24.** **Detroit Lions D/ST:** The Lions had minimal turnover from last season, but that may not exactly be a good thing. They averaged over 22 points against per game last season to go along with only had 26 sacks - one ahead of the last place Oakland Raiders in the statistic - and also only forced 14 turnovers. Despite playing Chicago in Week 15, the Lions are a risky defensive pick during the draft this year.

**25.** **New York Jets D/ST:** The Jets as a whole are predicted to struggle this year - as in compete for the number one overall pick struggle. Their defensive line is borderline elite, but the rest of the defense has glaring holes that are bound to be exploited. The pedestrian offense on the other side of the ball for the Jets only inhibits the D/ST unit more, and they are best left on the waiver wire to start the season off.

**26.** **Washington Redskins D/ST:** Washington got a great steal in Jonathan Allen in the draft and also added tackling specialist Zach Brown. That said, they needed to improve on their 377.9 yards against average last season, as well as their mediocre number of forced turnovers (20 total). The Redskins have a solid offense, but a tough schedule this season, and are best left alone in fantasy drafts.

| **26** | **_Washington Redskins D/ST_** | 377.9   | 23.9 | 38 | 7/17 | 13 | 0 | 1 |



**27.** **Dallas Cowboys D/ST:** It seems like everyone on the Cowboys’ defense left in the offseason or was suspended in some fashion. Barry Church and their two starting corners (Brandon Carr and Morris Claiborne) are all gone, leaving glaring holes in the secondary, and the Cowboys are hoping their offense can keep true to last year’s form - if Ezekiel Elliott can avoid an early suspension. They are a risky pick, and should barely be on the fantasy radar this year.

**28.** **Indianapolis Colts D/ST:** The Colts added a ton of new players to the roster on the defensive side of the ball this offseason, including Jabaal Sheard and Jonathan Hankins as well as rookie safety Malik Hooker, but should experience some growing paints his year as they come together as a unit. The Colts should be a good team this year due to their offense and having one of the [easiest schedules in the NFL this season](http://www.espn.com/blog/nflnation/post/_/id/234722/2017-nfl-strength-of-schedule), but it’s risky to take them in fantasy drafts.

**29.** **Chicago Bears D/ST:** While the Bears added Prince Amukamara to an already mediocre secondary,  they didn’t address enough to warrant real fantasy consideration this year. They had only 11 forced turnovers, and the offense will be bad enough to alone warrant avoiding the D/ST as a unit. Be wary.

**30.** **New Orleans Saints D/ST:** The Saints have usually been reliant on their powerful offense to lead them to victories in the past few years, and this year looks to be of minimal difference. They have a few talented pieces, but have yet to put it together in a solid fantasy campaign, forcing only 21 turnovers and nabbing only 30 sacks all of last season. It’s best left to avoid the Saints this year.

They are not exactly an ideal fantasy unit, and shouldn’t be on your radar in most drafts.

## **_DL:_**


**1.** **JJ Watt - Hou:** The otherworldly JJ Watt is returning (allegedly) healthy this season, and should compete for the NFL sack leader if he stays that way throughout the year’s entirety. He had at least 17.5 sacks in 3 of 4 seasons from 2012 to 2015 before missing most of the 2016 season to injury, but he is a top candidate to dominate the league again this year. He could be the first defensive player off the board in IDP leagues, and rightfully so.

| Rank  | Player Name  | Sacks      | QB Hurries         | Total Tackles | Fumbles Recovered  | Fumbles Forced | Passes Defended  |
| ------------- | ------------- |:-------------:| -----:| -----:| -----:| -----:| -----:|
| **1** | **_JJ Watt_** | 1.5   | <5 | 8 | 1 | 0 | 0 |



**2.** **Khalil Mack - Oak:** Khalil Mack, depending on the platform your league uses, could be a dual position player this season. While that is reliant on your site and the owners that be in such, what is not reliant on that is Mack’s on field production. He gets high numbers of both tackles and sacks, and is present on both running and passing downs. He is easily a top DL if eligible, but still a starting LB in IDP leagues.

| Rank  | Player Name  | Sacks      | QB Hurries         | Total Tackles | Fumbles Recovered  | Fumbles Forced | Passes Defended  |
| ------------- | ------------- |:-------------:| -----:| -----:| -----:| -----:| -----:|
| **2** | **_Khalil Mack_** | 11   | 25 | 73 | 3 | 5 | 3 |



**3.** **Jason Pierre-Paul - NYG:** JPP was a hot story in the 2015 offseason, but has continued his reign as a powerful lineman in the NFL with 7 sacks and 24 QB hurries last season. He remains the face of the defensive line in New York, and a viable candidate for double digit sacks again this year.

| Rank  | Player Name  | Sacks      | QB Hurries         | Total Tackles | Fumbles Recovered  | Fumbles Forced | Passes Defended  |
| ------------- | ------------- |:-------------:| -----:| -----:| -----:| -----:| -----:|
| **3** | **_Jason Pierre-Paul_** | 7   | 24 | 53 | 1 | 3 | 8 |



**4.** **Joey Bosa - LAC:** Second year Joey Bosa had a massively effective rookie year in which he compiled 10.5 sacks despite not playing a full 16 game season. The Chargers’ defense is an up and coming unit that has potential for solid QB pressure on an every down basis, thus bolstering Bosa’s ranking as a pass rusher. He could surprise many this season by even improving on his already astounding rookie year, but it would be a success for him to even match it. He is a DL1, no doubt.

| Rank  | Player Name  | Sacks      | QB Hurries         | Total Tackles | Fumbles Recovered  | Fumbles Forced | Passes Defended  |
| ------------- | ------------- |:-------------:| -----:| -----:| -----:| -----:| -----:|
| **4** | **_Joey Bosa_** | 10.5   | 23 | 41 | 0 | 0 | 0 |



**5.** **Olivier Vernon - NYG:** Olivier Vernon lines up opposite JPP along the Giants front, and was successful in both the sacks and tackles department last season. He has had at least 60 total tackles in 3 of the last 4 seasons while also accumulating 34 sacks in that span. He’s a low end DL1 due to his high floor.

| Rank  | Player Name  | Sacks      | QB Hurries         | Total Tackles | Fumbles Recovered  | Fumbles Forced | Passes Defended  |
| ------------- | ------------- |:-------------:| -----:| -----:| -----:| -----:| -----:|
| **5** | **_Olivier Vernon_** | 8.5   | 37 | 63 | 1 | 1 | 0 |



**6.** **Lorenzo Alexander - Buf:** Lorenzo Alexander may or may not be designated for a DL eligible spot in your fantasy league, but if he is, he is worth fantasy gold. A breakout candidate last year despite his veteran status, Alexander had 12.5 sacks and over 70 total tackles. If your league allows Alexander as a DL eligible player, he is a DL1 all day - especially if your league counts tackles.

| Rank  | Player Name  | Sacks      | QB Hurries         | Total Tackles | Fumbles Recovered  | Fumbles Forced | Passes Defended  |
| ------------- | ------------- |:-------------:| -----:| -----:| -----:| -----:| -----:|
| **6** | **_Lorenzo Alexander_** | 12.5   | 17 | 76 | 0 | 3 | 6 |



**7.** **Danielle Hunter - Min:** Danielle Hunter broke out in a big way last season, with 56 total tackles and 12.5 sacks to his name last year. Jim McCormack at ESPN noted that Hunter led all players with at least 500 snaps in sacks per snap last season, and this stat only helps his fantasy value. Hunter has double digit sack potential on a stout Vikings defense, and could improve on his other stats to boot. He’s a DL2 with a lot of upside.

**8.** **Vic Beasley, Jr. - Atl:** Vic Beasley was among the major breakout players on the defensive side of the ball in 2016. He amassed a whopping 15.5 sacks, and added 6 forced fumbles to the mix as he made his presence known on the Atlanta defensive front. With an improved Atlanta defense this year - including first round pick Tak McKinley - Beasley could again wreak havoc for the Falcons as a top level DL1. He’s a sleeper pick going this low at the position.

**9.** **Jadeveon Clowney - Hou:** Jadeveon Clowney could break out in a big way this year, and it could pay big fantasy dividends if he is eligible for a DL spot in your IDP league After only 6 sacks and 18 QB hurries all of last season, a healthy JJ Watt and the addition of rookie linebacker Zach Cunningham could take enough blocking attention away from Clowney to make him a force in the sack department. Houston’s defense as a whole should improve with Watt coming back to full strength, but that alone makes Clowney a low level DL1 with upside. This could be the year we finally see the emergence of the 2014 first overall pick come through in the sack column.

**10.** **Aaron Donald - LAR:** The rare fantasy asset at defensive tackle, Donald has had at least 8 sacks and 47 tackles in each of his three seasons in the NFL. He won’t blow you out of the water with his numbers due to his position, but is still as reliable as they come on the defensive front in fantasy leagues. He’s a reliable DL2 with a high floor and low ceiling.

While he has never had a double digit sack season in his entire career, Campbell is a reliable tackle/sack combo lineman in fantasy that will surely keep your team afloat. He’s a reliable DL2 when it comes to fantasy purposes.

He’s a rock solid DL2.

He likely won’t hit double digit sacks, but he’ll get close enough and get enough tackles to compete at the position. He’s a low end DL1 for fantasy purposes.

## **_LB:_**

**1.** **Kwon Alexander - TB:** With 145 tackles last season Kwon Alexander became a solid centerpiece of the Tampa Bay defense. He should get better in his 3rd NFL season this year, and he is a top LB1 to take in fantasy drafts.

| Rank  | Player Name  | Total Tackles      | Sacks   | QB Hurries | Fumbles Recovered  | Fumbles Forced | Passes Defended  | Interceptions |
| ------------- | ------------- |:-------------:| -----:| -----:| -----:| -----:| -----:| -----:|
| **1** | **_Kwon Alexander_** | 145  | 3 | 6 | 1 | 1 | 7 | 1 |


**2.** **Luke Kuechly - Car:** Kuechly is a tackle machine, but cannot be relied on for much more than that. That said, the amount of tackles he gets (153 or more in 3 of his 5 seasons) makes him a top fantasy LB. A solid 9+ a week from tackles alone is more than enough to ask for your starting linebacker.

| Rank  | Player Name  | Total Tackles      | Sacks   | QB Hurries | Fumbles Recovered  | Fumbles Forced | Passes Defended  | Interceptions |
| ------------- | ------------- |:-------------:| -----:| -----:| -----:| -----:| -----:| -----:|

**3.** **Bobby Wagner - Sea:** Bobby Wagner exploded for 167 combined tackles last season, and added 4.5 sacks to that number to propel himself into relevance for IDP linebackers. He’s now a top option at the core of a tough Seattle defense, and his tackles alone make him startle each week. He’s a quality LB1.

**4.** **Alec Ogletree - LAR** Ogletree had 136 tackles last season, and will be a main part of the Rams defense again this season. He’s only got 3.5 sacks and 5 interceptions on his career, so the tackles are what provide Ogletree’s main value. He is a high end LB2 this year in most formats.

**5.** **Telvin Smith - Jac:** Telvin Smith has recorded over 100 tackles in all three seasons he has been in the NFL. He’s also recorded 5.5 sacks and 4 interceptions in that span - including 8 passes defended last year alone - to show that he’s not just a tackle-reliant linebacker. He’s got good upside in an up and coming Jaguars defense, and comes into the season as a good LB2.

**6.** **Jamie Collins - Cle:** Collins steps into a major role in the Cleveland defense, and should put up good numbers as an every down linebacker. The Browns defense could be on the field more than they’d like, and Collins will be in the middle of every play. He’s an LB1 in fantasy this season.

**7.** **CJ Mosley - Bal:** Mosley had 92 tackles last season, but his 4 interceptions are what set him apart from many other linebackers. He won’t light up the stat sheet, as his most productive season tackle-wise was his rookie year in 2014 and his numbers overall have decreased by the season, but he’s a reliable bench linebacker who will be on the field for almost every down, and provides opportunity for the unpredictable defensive touchdowns via his passing game prowess.

**9.** **Ryan Shazier - Pit:** Shazier could be one of those players who is better on the field than on the stat sheet, as he has had mediocre numbers of both tackles, sacks, and other stats in past seasons. One aspect Shazier does offer upside is on passing downs, where he had 3 interceptions and 9 passes defended last year. Turnovers are opportunities for the sporadic and elusive defensive touchdown, so Shazier is a high upside pick as an LB1, but makes a top level LB2.

While he’s got potential to be a top level fantasy linebacker, you may want to look at someone a little more reliable that early. That said, he’s still an LB1.

**14.** **Lavonte David - TB:** Last season was a sporadic down season for David, who had recorded at least 139 tackles in each of his first four NFL seasons prior to 2016. While he did still have 5 sacks last year, his tackle totals plummeted, and Kwon Alexander emerged as a force in his own right to take those opportunities away from David. Regardless, David is a great bounce back candidate this year at LB, and should perform way closer to his usual numbers than last year’s poor showing (by his standards), and is a sleeper LB2.

He’s a high upside LB2 this year.

He’s a good sleeper pick this low, but don’t rely on him as a starter for fantasy purposes until he can prove consistency.

He is arguably the best sack artist in the NFL, and if he counts as a dual DL/LB, his value shoots way higher than this. As a sole LB, he’s still worth a roster spot due to the sack upside he brings.

**39.** **Reggie Ragland - Buf:** Reggie Ragland had extremely high hopes as a rookie, but tore his ACL during training camp and missed his entire rookie season. He steps into a new look Bills defense under new coach Sean McDermott, and is a good sleeper pick this season. Don’t rely on him as any more than a bench player on draft day, however.

**40.** **Justin Houston - KC:** Justin Houston is a Von Miller-esque type of linebacker in fantasy, as he’s never had 70 total tackles in a season in his 6 years in the NFL. He has, however, put up double digit sack numbers in three of those six - including a 22 sack explosion in 2014. He’s coming off a partial season (5 games) due to injury, but he’s only 28 and still capable of putting up huge sack totals. He’s a great sleeper pick this low and definitely worth a LB roster spot.

**41.** **Darron Lee- NYJ:** Lee enters his second year after playing a fairly decent role for the Jets last year. He recorded 73 tackles and a sack, and should improve on both numbers this season. The Jets defense should be on the field a lot, giving him more opportunity to get points, but don’t rely on him as a starter this year.

**42.** **Whitney Mercilus - Hou:** Mercilus is a high upside LB that could be taken later in drafts, and his 23 QB hurries are a good indicator of his potential in the sack department.

## **_DB:_**


**1.** **Landon Collins - NYG:** Collins is hands down the best DB in IDP formats. With a ridiculous 237 tackles in his first two seasons in the NFL, he added 4 sacks and 5 interceptions (as well as 13 passes defended) to his repertoire this past year. He could be the first defensive player off the board in some IDP drafts, and may be worth it.

| Rank  | Player Name  | Total Tackles      | Interceptions   | Passes Defended | Fumbles Recovered  | Fumbles Forced | Sacks  |
| ------------- | ------------- |:-------------:| -----:| -----:| -----:| -----:| -----:|
| **1** | **_Landon Collins_** | 125   | 5 | 13 | 1 | 0 | 4 |



**2.** **Keanu Neal - Atl:** Neal was thrust into a prime role as a rookie, and he performed admirably with 106 tackles and 8 passes defended. The Falcons’ defense as a whole should take a step forward this year, and Neal could be at the forefront of that improvement. He’s a DB1 this year due to his upside and already established role.

| Rank  | Player Name  | Total Tackles      | Interceptions   | Passes Defended | Fumbles Recovered  | Fumbles Forced | Sacks  |
| ------------- | ------------- |:-------------:| -----:| -----:| -----:| -----:| -----:|
| **2** | **_Keanu Neal_** | 106   | 0 | 8 | 1 | 5 | 0 |



**3.** **Harrison Smith - Min:** Harrison Smith has been a solid IDP selection since he came into the NFL in 2012, and his 91 tackles last year only cements that status. He could be going higher than this ranking, and his 7.5 sacks and 12 interceptions over his 5 seasons gives him DB1 upside. He’s got an extremely high floor among DB’s, and should be taken with confidence.

| Rank  | Player Name  | Total Tackles      | Interceptions   | Passes Defended | Fumbles Recovered  | Fumbles Forced | Sacks  |
| ------------- | ------------- |:-------------:| -----:| -----:| -----:| -----:| -----:|
| **3** | **_Harrison Smith_** | 91   | 0 | 2 | 1 | 0 | 2 |



**4.** **Johnathan Cyprien - Ten:** Cyprien moves from the Jaguars to the Titans this offseason, and joins a Tennessee unit that could be ready to take a big step forward this year behind an already potent offense. Cyprien has had at least 103 tackles in each of his first four seasons, and is a surefire DB1 in fantasy leagues this year.

| Rank  | Player Name  | Total Tackles      | Interceptions   | Passes Defended | Fumbles Recovered  | Fumbles Forced | Sacks  |
| ------------- | ------------- |:-------------:| -----:| -----:| -----:| -----:| -----:|
| **4** | **_Johnathan Cyprien_** | 128   | 0 | 4 | 1 | 1 | 1 |



**5.** **Tony Jefferson - Bal:** Jefferson moves from an already successful role in Arizona to a historically fruitful (for fantasy purposes) role in Baltimore. jefferson had 96 combined tackles last season, and is a threat in the sack department as well with two in each of the last two seasons. He’s a solid DB1 that could fit nicely into his new defense that faces 2017 opponents who last year had a [combined winning percentage of .471%](http://www.espn.com/blog/nflnation/post/_/id/234722/2017-nfl-strength-of-schedule).

| Rank  | Player Name  | Total Tackles      | Interceptions   | Passes Defended | Fumbles Recovered  | Fumbles Forced | Sacks  |
| ------------- | ------------- |:-------------:| -----:| -----:| -----:| -----:| -----:|
| **5** | **_Tony Jefferson_** | 96   | 0 | 5 | 2 | 2 | 2 |



**6.** **Morgan Burnett - GB:** The veteran Burnett should again play a big role in the Packers’ defense this season, and his IDP value also holds as he continued strong with another 93 tackles last season. He added 2 interceptions, 3 sacks, and an incredible 29 passes defended. Those stats make him a high end DB2 with DB1 upside.

| Rank  | Player Name  | Total Tackles      | Interceptions   | Passes Defended | Fumbles Recovered  | Fumbles Forced | Sacks  |
| ------------- | ------------- |:-------------:| -----:| -----:| -----:| -----:| -----:|
| **6** | **_Morgan Burnett_** | 93   | 2 | 29| 1 | 0 | 3 |



**7.** **Reshad Jones - Mia:** Jones missed most of the season last year, but is still a top IDP defensive back whenever he is healthy. He is a rare find that can perform in the tackle, sack, and interception departments, and should step back into his role as a mainstay on the Dolphins defense. He’s a top DB again this year.

| Rank  | Player Name  | Total Tackles      | Interceptions   | Passes Defended | Fumbles Recovered  | Fumbles Forced | Sacks  |
| ------------- | ------------- |:-------------:| -----:| -----:| -----:| -----:| -----:|

**8.** **Barry Church - Jac:** Veteran Barry Church jumped ship from a Dallas Cowboys team that made the playoffs last season to a Jacksonville squad that is still waiting to break out. The defense in front of him, however, could actually do it this year. The Jaguars are finally putting pieces together, and perhaps Church and his 434 tackles in the last 4 seasons could be the glue that holds it all together. He’s a DB1 in IDP fantasy formats.

| Rank  | Player Name  | Total Tackles      | Interceptions   | Passes Defended | Fumbles Recovered  | Fumbles Forced | Sacks  |
| ------------- | ------------- |:-------------:| -----:| -----:| -----:| -----:| -----:|
| **8** | **_Barry Church_** | 85   | 2 | 4 | 0 | 1 | 0 |



**9.** **TJ Ward - Den:** TJ Ward has been another reliable IDP selection since he came into the league with (surprisingly) Cleveland back in 2010. Last season in Denver he had a solid 87 tackles, and his sack numbers are also solid for a DB since coming to the Rockies (5 in 3 seasons). Ward is a reliable DB2 for fantasy purposes.

**10.** **Ha Ha Clinton-Dix - GB:** Clinton-Dix is an underrated IDP player, having never had less than 80 tackles in a season and with 4.5 sacks and 8 interceptions to go on his 3 year NFL career. Five of those interceptions came last year, exemplifying his improvement in the passing game, and he should be considered a prime sleeper pick at the DB position, especially this low. He has DB2 upside.

**11.** **Kurt Coleman - Car:** Coleman has had over 90 tackles in each of his 2 seasons in Carolina, and added 11 interceptions in that time span to boot. The Panthers’ defense should be improved from their struggle last season, and Coleman should be a solid candidate to repeat his performance from the past two seasons. He’s a high upside DB2.

Weddle also had 4 interceptions and 13 passed defended last year, giving him potential for opportunities to make plays on the ball. He’s a high upside DB2 in fantasy.

He is still a centerpiece of the Saints defense, but he’ll need to show a bit of improvement to justify such a high ranking at the position. He’s a reliable DB2 in 2017.

The Raiders defense as a whole is nothing to write home about (save for Khalil Mack), but Joseph is a rising star on that side of the ball. While he shouldn’t post top numbers this year, expect his stats last year to improve with more experience and for him to be a solid DB2 this season.

He’s a reliable DB2 for fantasy this year.

**16.** **Kam Chancellor - Sea:** Chancellor is more of a big name safety than a stat sheet hog in fantasy football, but nonetheless he is still reliable player to have on your roster. He has had 100 or more total tackles just once in his 7 year career (2012), but still provides enough awareness to be relevant as a low level DB1 in fantasy, but be sure you don’t overdraft him.

While his position as a cornerback restricts him from true fantasy value, he has had 166 tackles in the last two seasons combined to go along with 6 interceptions. Ryan is one of the few cornerbacks worth rostering in IDP leagues.

He’s a good late round flier as a sleeper pick at DB.

Addae is part of an up and coming defense in Los Angeles, but shouldn’t be trusted as a low ceiling DB2 in fantasy formats.
